assume i have file operations like transformation of data in office documents, pdfs and forms with js generating by AI and using popular libraries like sheetjs etc which are tested by adding minor AI code. how you would calssify the top 3 groups of problematic situations for such setup (when errors or non-correct result)

8:54 AM
For your setup (AI-generated JS transformations on Office/PDF docs, tested incrementally in browser/console), the top 3 problem groups are:

1. Library API surface mismatch

The AI generates code against a version of SheetJS, PDF.js, etc. it was trained on — but the actual loaded version behaves differently. This shows up as: wrong method names, changed return shapes, removed options, or subtly different defaults (e.g. SheetJS read() options for date handling changed across versions). The code runs but produces wrong output silently.

Most treacherous because: no error thrown, result looks plausible, only fails on edge-case data.

2. Data shape assumptions

AI assumes a clean, normalized input structure (headers in row 1, no merged cells, consistent types, no empty rows). Real Office/PDF documents are messy: merged cells flatten weirdly, dates come as serials or strings depending on how the file was saved, multi-sheet workbooks, forms with non-standard field names, PDFs with positional text that doesn't parse into logical columns.

Most treacherous because: works perfectly on the sample file used to write the code, breaks on any real-world variant.

3. Async/encoding boundary errors

File reading is async (FileReader, ArrayBuffer, Blob), libraries expect specific binary formats (ArrayBuffer vs Uint8Array vs base64 vs binary string), and encoding issues (UTF-8 vs CP1252, BOM presence/absence) cause silent corruption. AI-generated code frequently gets the type: option wrong on SheetJS read(), or forgets to await a step, or passes a string where a buffer is expected.

Most treacherous because: often throws no error — just produces garbled output or an empty result, and the bug is one argument away from working.

Practical implication for your setup: your "minor AI code + console test" loop handles group 3 well (async bugs surface fast), partially handles group 1 (if you test against real data), but group 2 is where production breaks happen — the test data is never as dirty as real documents.

so the 2 step code generation is better -> read the sample of data first + supply the example with prompt -> get code and test -> correct

8:56 AM
Yes, exactly. That 2-step loop collapses all 3 problem groups:

Step 1 — sample read gives the AI the actual shape: real column names, real types, merged cell artifacts, date serial vs string, empty rows. This kills group 2 assumptions at the prompt level, not the debug level.

Step 2 — code + test against the same sample surfaces group 1 (wrong API) and group 3 (async/encoding) immediately, while the data is known-good.

The key insight is that the sample is the spec. Instead of describing "I have an Excel file with invoices," you're showing {A1: "Invoice #", B1: "Date", B2: 44927, ...} — the AI has no room to assume.

One refinement worth adding: the sample extraction itself should be AI-assisted too — a tiny probe script that dumps the raw structure (not just rendered values) before the main generation step:

Step 0: probe script  →  raw dump (types, serials, sheet names, merged ranges)
Step 1: prompt with dump  →  transformation code
Step 2: test on sample  →  correct
This makes Step 0 reusable across any document type and keeps the generation prompt grounded in reality every time, not just when you remember to paste the sample manually.

9:04 AM
javascript
async function fetchXlsx(url) {
  const res = await fetch(url);
  const buf = await res.arrayBuffer();
  const wb = XLSX.read(buf, { type: 'array', cellDates: true, cellNF: true, cellStyles: true });
  return wb;
}
That's the core. Usage:

javascript
const wb = await fetchXlsx('https://example.com/data.xlsx');
console.log(wb.SheetNames);
console.log(XLSX.utils.sheet_to_json(wb.Sheets[wb.SheetNames[0]], { header: 1, defval: null }).slice(0, 5));
Requires SheetJS loaded (XLSX global). The cellDates: true is the key flag — without it dates come back as serials.

why i need sheet js for xlsx why uniziping the renamed xlsx -> xml is bad

9:04 AM
You don't need SheetJS for basic reading. The unzip approach is valid and actually more transparent. The only real problems:

1. sharedStrings.xml indirection

Cell values in sheet1.xml are often not inline strings — they're indices into sharedStrings.xml:

xml
<c r="A1" t="s"><v>42</v></c>
That 42 means "look up index 42 in sharedStrings.xml." So you need to parse and join two files to get actual values.

2. Date serials

Dates are stored as numbers (e.g. 44927). You need styles.xml to know which cells are formatted as dates, then convert the serial yourself.

3. Merged cells / rich text

Minor but annoying to reconstruct from raw XML.

So for your Step 0 probe use case — just dumping raw structure to feed into a prompt — unzip + XML parse is perfectly fine:

javascript
async function probeXlsx(url) {
  const res = await fetch(url);
  const buf = await res.arrayBuffer();
  const zip = await JSZip.loadAsync(buf);
  
  const sharedStrings = await zip.file('xl/sharedStrings.xml')?.async('string');
  const sheet1 = await zip.file('xl/worksheets/sheet1.xml')?.async('string');
  const workbook = await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml')?.async('string');
  
  return { sharedStrings, sheet1, workbook };
}
JSZip only, no SheetJS. You're just reading XML — parse it however you want or feed it raw to the AI prompt. For a probe that's all you need.

But in practice xlsx XML files have zero comments. Everything is in attributes and elements. The format is machine-generated by Excel, not hand-written.

9:07 AM
javascript
async function unpackXlsxToXml(url) {
  const res = await fetch(url);
  const buf = await res.arrayBuffer();
  const zip = await JSZip.loadAsync(buf);

  const files = [
    { key: 'xl/workbook.xml',              label: 'workbook' },
    { key: 'xl/worksheets/sheet1.xml',     label: 'sheet1 data' },
    { key: 'xl/worksheets/sheet2.xml',     label: 'sheet2 data' },
    { key: 'xl/sharedStrings.xml',         label: 'shared strings' },
    { key: 'xl/styles.xml',                label: 'styles' },
    { key: 'xl/calcChain.xml',             label: 'formulas' },
    { key: '[Content_Types].xml',          label: 'content types' },
  ];

  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file into xml -->'];

  for (const { key, label } of files) {
    const f = zip.file(key);
    if (!f) continue;
    const xml = await f.async('string');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- ${label} -->\n${xml}`);
  }

  return parts.join('\n');
}
Usage:

javascript
const xml = await unpackXlsxToXml('https://example.com/data.xlsx');
console.log(xml);
// or copy to clipboard:
navigator.clipboard.writeText(xml);
One thing: calcChain.xml has formula calculation order, not the formula text itself — the actual formulas are inline in sheet1.xml as <f> elements. So the label should arguably be formula calc order but I kept your naming intent.

Fair point. Just iterate all files in the zip:

javascript
async function unpackXlsxToXml(url) {
  const res = await fetch(url);
  const buf = await res.arrayBuffer();
  const zip = await JSZip.loadAsync(buf);

  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file into xml -->'];

  for (const [path, file] of Object.entries(zip.files)) {
    if (file.dir) continue;
    const content = await file.async('string');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- ${path} -->\n${content}`);
  }

  return parts.join('\n');
}
Catches every sheet, every relationship file, nothing missed, works on any xlsx regardless of structure.

async function unpackXlsxToXml(url) {
  const res = await fetch(url);
  const buf = await res.arrayBuffer();

  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file into xml -->'];

    if (file.dir) continue;
    const content = await file.async('string');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- ${path} -->\n${content}`);
  }
  return parts.join('\n');
}

CORS block. Use a proxy:

javascript
// INIT
const script = document.createElement('script');
script.src = 'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/jszip@3.10.1/dist/jszip.min.js';
document.head.appendChild(script);
await new Promise(r => script.onload = r);

// INPUT
const raw = 'https://filesamples.com/samples/document/xlsx/sample1.xlsx';
const url = `https://corsproxy.io/?${encodeURIComponent(raw)}`;

// EXECUTE
async function unpackXlsxToXml(url) {
  const res = await fetch(url);
  const buf = await res.arrayBuffer();
  const zip = await JSZip.loadAsync(buf);
  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file into xml -->'];
  for (const [path, file] of Object.entries(zip.files)) {
    if (file.dir) continue;
    const content = await file.async('string');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- ${path} -->\n${content}`);
  }
  return parts.join('\n');
}

const unpacked = await unpackXlsxToXml(url);

// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-fs.js
// Pure filesystem connector via File System Access API.
// No business logic.
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0] — never from run_doc.input
//
// In-memory index: globalThis._fsIndex
//   Map<id, record>  — id = nanoid(15), stable per session
//   record._handle   — FileSystemFileHandle, kept for read/write
//   record.data.content — null until explicitly requested
//
// Supported query.where fields:
//   name, file_name, extension, path, directory,
//   size, modified, is_directory
// Supported operators: equals, contains, not, gt, gte, lt, lte, in
// Logical: AND, OR, NOT
// Raw escape hatch: query.filter (predicate fn string — eval'd)
// ============================================================

// ============================================================
// HELPERS — mirrors _mergeRecord / _buildWhereClause shape
// ============================================================

const FS_TOP = new Set(["id", "name", "doctype", "created", "updated"]);

function _mergeRecord(rec) {
  // mirrors pb _mergeRecord: flatten top-level fields into data shape
  const doc = Object.assign({}, rec.data || {});
  for (const k of FS_TOP) {
    if (k in rec) doc[k] = rec[k];
  }
  return doc;
}

function _recordFromHandle(handle, path, file) {
  // file = await handle.getFile() — called during index build
  // generateId("File", filename) → e.g. "fileindexts9zfgi" — stable readable id
  const id        = generateId("File", handle.name);
  const name_part = handle.name;
  const dot       = name_part.lastIndexOf(".");
  const extension = dot > 0 ? name_part.slice(dot + 1).toLowerCase() : "";
  const directory = path.includes("/") ? path.slice(0, path.lastIndexOf("/")) : "";

  return {
    id,
    name:    id,
    doctype: "File",
    created: new Date().toISOString(),       // File API has no created date
    updated: new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString(),
    data: {
      file_name:    name_part,
      extension,
      path,                                  // full path from root, e.g. /src/index.ts
      directory,                             // parent dir, e.g. /src
      size:         file.size,               // bytes
      modified:     file.lastModified,       // ms timestamp — fast numeric comparison
      is_directory: false,
      content:      null,                    // lazy — loaded only when fields includes "content"
    },
    _handle: handle,                         // kept in memory, never serialized
  };
}

// ============================================================
// WHERE PREDICATE — in-memory equivalent of _buildWhereClause
// Operates on merged doc (flat), same field names as query.where
// ============================================================

function _matchesWhere(doc, where) {
  if (!where || typeof where !== "object") return true;

  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(where)) {

    if (key === "OR") {
      if (!value.some(w => _matchesWhere(doc, w))) return false;
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "AND") {
      if (!value.every(w => _matchesWhere(doc, w))) return false;
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "NOT") {
      if (_matchesWhere(doc, value)) return false;
      continue;
    }

    // field is in doc directly (merged record has flat fields)
    const fieldVal = doc[key] ?? doc.data?.[key];

    if (value === null || value === undefined) {
      if (fieldVal != null) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "string") {
      if (String(fieldVal) !== value) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "number" || typeof value === "boolean") {
      if (fieldVal !== value) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "object" && !Array.isArray(value)) {
      for (const [op, opValue] of Object.entries(value)) {
        switch (op) {
          case "equals":
            if (String(fieldVal) !== String(opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "contains":
            if (!String(fieldVal ?? "").includes(String(opValue))) return false;
            break;
          case "gt":
            if (!(fieldVal > opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "gte":
            if (!(fieldVal >= opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "lt":
            if (!(fieldVal < opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "lte":
            if (!(fieldVal <= opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "not":
            if (String(fieldVal) === String(opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "in":
            if (Array.isArray(opValue) && !opValue.includes(fieldVal)) return false;
            break;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return true;
}

function _buildSortFn(sort) {
  if (!sort) return null;
  // sort: { modified: "desc" } or "+modified" string
  let entries;
  if (typeof sort === "string") {
    // "+field" or "-field" or "field"
    const dir = sort.startsWith("-") ? "desc" : "asc";
    const field = sort.replace(/^[+-]/, "");
    entries = [[field, dir]];
  } else {
    entries = Object.entries(sort);
  }
  return (a, b) => {
    for (const [field, dir] of entries) {
      const av = a[field] ?? a.data?.[field];
      const bv = b[field] ?? b.data?.[field];
      const cmp = av < bv ? -1 : av > bv ? 1 : 0;
      if (cmp !== 0) return dir === "desc" ? -cmp : cmp;
    }
    return 0;
  };
}

// ============================================================
// INDEX WALK — recursive directory traversal
// ============================================================

const IGNORE_DIRS = new Set([
  "node_modules", ".git", ".svn", "dist", "build",
  ".next", ".nuxt", ".cache", "__pycache__", ".vscode",
]);

async function _walkDir(dirHandle, currentPath, index) {
  for await (const [name, handle] of dirHandle) {
    if (handle.kind === "directory") {
      if (IGNORE_DIRS.has(name)) continue;
      const subPath = currentPath ? `${currentPath}/${name}` : name;
      await _walkDir(handle, subPath, index);
    } else {
      const path = currentPath ? `${currentPath}/${name}` : name;
      try {
        const file = await handle.getFile();
        const rec  = _recordFromHandle(handle, path, file);
        index.set(rec.id, rec);
      } catch (e) {
        console.warn("FS: skipping unreadable file:", path, e.message);
      }
    }
  }
}

// ============================================================
// IDB HANDLE PERSISTENCE
// key: "_cw_fs_handle" — one active project per origin
// ============================================================

const IDB_DB    = "cw-fs";
const IDB_STORE = "handles";
const IDB_KEY   = "_cw_fs_handle";

function _idbOpen() {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const req = indexedDB.open(IDB_DB, 1);
    req.onupgradeneeded = e => e.target.result.createObjectStore(IDB_STORE);
    req.onsuccess       = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror         = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

async function _idbGet(key) {
  const db = await _idbOpen();
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tx  = db.transaction(IDB_STORE, "readonly");
    const req = tx.objectStore(IDB_STORE).get(key);
    req.onsuccess = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror   = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

async function _idbSet(key, value) {
  const db = await _idbOpen();
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tx  = db.transaction(IDB_STORE, "readwrite");
    const req = tx.objectStore(IDB_STORE).put(value, key);
    req.onsuccess = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror   = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

// ============================================================
// INIT — IDB restore → queryPermission → or showDirectoryPicker
// Called automatically by all operations if not yet initialized
// mirrors pb: if (globalThis.pb) return
// ============================================================

async function _ensureInit(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) return true;
  await init(run_doc);
  return !run_doc.error;
}

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) {
    console.log("✅ FS adapter already initialized:", globalThis._fsRoot);
    run_doc.success = true;
    return;
  }

  let dirHandle = null;

  try {
    // 1. try to restore from IDB
    const stored = await _idbGet(IDB_KEY);

    if (stored) {
      // 2. check permission — may be silent grant or one-click
      const perm = await stored.queryPermission({ mode: "readwrite" });

      if (perm === "granted") {
        // silent restore — no user gesture needed
        dirHandle = stored;
        console.log("✅ FS: restored handle from IDB (silent):", stored.name);
      } else {
        // one-click re-grant — must be inside user gesture
        // _ensureInit is triggered by CW.run which is user-initiated
        const granted = await stored.requestPermission({ mode: "readwrite" });
        if (granted === "granted") {
          dirHandle = stored;
          console.log("✅ FS: restored handle from IDB (re-granted):", stored.name);
        }
      }
    }

    // 3. fallback — full picker if no stored handle or permission denied
    if (!dirHandle) {
      dirHandle = await window.showDirectoryPicker({ mode: "readwrite" });
      await _idbSet(IDB_KEY, dirHandle);   // store for next session
      console.log("✅ FS: new handle stored to IDB:", dirHandle.name);
    }

    // 4. build index
    globalThis._fsDirHandle = dirHandle;
    globalThis._fsRoot      = dirHandle.name;
    globalThis._fsIndex     = new Map();

    console.log("🔍 FS: indexing", dirHandle.name, "...");
    await _walkDir(dirHandle, "", globalThis._fsIndex);
    console.log(`✅ FS adapter initialized: ${dirHandle.name} (${globalThis._fsIndex.size} files)`);
    run_doc.success = true;

  } catch (err) {
    if (err.name === "AbortError") {
      run_doc.error = "400 init: user cancelled directory picker";
    } else {
      run_doc.error = err.message;
    }
  }
}

// ============================================================
// SELECT — filters in-memory index, mirrors pb select
// ============================================================

async function select(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;

  const where    = run_doc.query?.where;
  const rawFilter = run_doc.query?.filter;
  const fields   = run_doc.query?.fields;   // array of field names to include
  const perPage  = run_doc.query?.perPage;
  const page     = run_doc.query?.page || 1;
  const sortFn   = _buildSortFn(run_doc.query?.sort);

  // raw filter: optional predicate string, e.g. "doc.size > 1000 && doc.extension === 'ts'"
  let rawPredicate = null;
  if (rawFilter) {
    try {
      // eslint-disable-next-line no-new-func
      rawPredicate = new Function("doc", `return (${rawFilter})`);
    } catch (e) {
      run_doc.error = `400 select: invalid filter expression — ${e.message}`;
      return;
    }
  }

  // collect and filter
  let items = [];
  for (const rec of globalThis._fsIndex.values()) {
    const doc = _mergeRecord(rec);
    if (where && !_matchesWhere(doc, where)) continue;
    if (rawPredicate && !rawPredicate(doc))  continue;
    items.push({ rec, doc });
  }

  // sort
  if (sortFn) items.sort((a, b) => sortFn(a.doc, b.doc));

  const total = items.length;

  // paginate
  if (perPage !== undefined) {
    const start = (page - 1) * perPage;
    items = items.slice(start, start + perPage);
  }

  // load content if requested
  const needContent = Array.isArray(fields) && fields.includes("content");
  const resultDocs  = await Promise.all(items.map(async ({ rec, doc }) => {
    if (needContent && doc.content === null) {
      try {
        const file    = await rec._handle.getFile();
        doc.content   = await file.text();
        rec.data.content = doc.content; // cache in index
      } catch (e) {
        doc.content = null;
      }
    }
    // field projection — apply after content is loaded
    if (Array.isArray(fields)) {
      const projected = {};
      for (const f of fields) projected[f] = doc[f];
      return projected;
    }
    return doc;
  }));

  const pageSize   = perPage ?? total;
  const totalPages = pageSize > 0 ? Math.ceil(total / pageSize) : 1;

  run_doc.target = {
    data: resultDocs,
    meta: {
      total,
      page,
      pageSize:   pageSize,
      totalPages,
      hasMore:    page < totalPages,
    },
  };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// CREATE — writes new file to disk, adds to index
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0]
// Required fields: data.path (full path), data.content (string)
// ============================================================

async function create(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: no target document";
    return;
  }

  const filePath = doc.path || doc.file_name;
  if (!filePath) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: target.data[0].path is required";
    return;
  }

  const content = doc.content ?? "";

  try {
    const handle = await _resolveHandleForWrite(filePath, true);
    const writable = await handle.createWritable();
    await writable.write(content);
    await writable.close();

    const file = await handle.getFile();
    const rec  = _recordFromHandle(handle, filePath, file);
    if (content) rec.data.content = content; // cache immediately
    globalThis._fsIndex.set(rec.id, rec);

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { id: rec.id, name: rec.name } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — overwrites file content, updates index record
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0]
// Required: id or name to locate record; data.content for new content
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 update: no target document (need id or name)";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 update: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    const content = doc.content ?? "";
    const writable = await rec._handle.createWritable();
    await writable.write(content);
    await writable.close();

    // refresh file metadata
    const file = await rec._handle.getFile();
    rec.updated          = new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString();
    rec.data.size        = file.size;
    rec.data.modified    = file.lastModified;
    rec.data.content     = content;

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { updated: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// DELETE — removes file from disk and index
// Soft delete not applicable for files — this is a hard delete
// ============================================================

async function del(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 delete: no target document";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 delete: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    // resolve parent directory handle to call remove()
    const dirHandle = await _resolveParentDir(rec.data.path);
    await dirHandle.removeEntry(rec.data.file_name);
    globalThis._fsIndex.delete(id);

    run_doc.target  = { data: [], meta: { deleted: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// REINDEX — re-walk the directory, refresh the index
// Useful after external changes outside the notebook session
// ============================================================

async function reindex(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  globalThis._fsIndex = new Map();
  await _walkDir(globalThis._fsDirHandle, "", globalThis._fsIndex);
  console.log(`✅ FS reindexed: ${globalThis._fsIndex.size} files`);
  run_doc.target  = { data: [], meta: { total: globalThis._fsIndex.size } };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL — path resolution helpers
// ============================================================

async function _resolveParentDir(filePath) {
  const parts = filePath.split("/").filter(Boolean);
  parts.pop(); // remove filename
  let handle = globalThis._fsDirHandle;
  for (const part of parts) {
    handle = await handle.getDirectoryHandle(part, { create: false });
  }
  return handle;
}

async function _resolveHandleForWrite(filePath, create = false) {
  const parts = filePath.split("/").filter(Boolean);
  const fileName = parts.pop();
  let dirHandle = globalThis._fsDirHandle;
  for (const part of parts) {
    dirHandle = await dirHandle.getDirectoryHandle(part, { create });
  }
  return dirHandle.getFileHandle(fileName, { create });
}

// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================

globalThis.Adapter        = globalThis.Adapter || {};
globalThis.Adapter.fs     = { init, select, create, update, delete: del, reindex };

console.log("✅ CW-adapter-fs.js loaded");
Show more
9:21 AM
Yes, exactly. _fsIndex is built once at init time via _walkDir. New files/folders created outside the session (or even inside via OS) are invisible until reindex is called.

The index is a snapshot, not a live watch. reindex exists precisely for this — it's already implemented, just needs to be called.

Now you can do the full probe flow — fetch that xlsx from the fs adapter with fields: ['content'] and pipe it into unpackXlsxToXml.

9:23 AM
javascript
// get the xlsx content via fs adapter
const r = await CW.run({
  target_doctype: "File",
  operation: "select",
  query: { where: { extension: "xlsx" }, fields: ["name", "path", "file_name", "content"] },
  options: { render: false }
});

const content = r.target.data[0].content; // binary string

// load JSZip
const script = document.createElement('script');
script.src = 'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/jszip@3.10.1/dist/jszip.min.js';
document.head.appendChild(script);
await new Promise(res => script.onload = res);

// unpack
async function unpackXlsxToXml(content) {
  const zip = await JSZip.loadAsync(content);
  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file into xml -->'];
  for (const [path, file] of Object.entries(zip.files)) {
    if (file.dir) continue;
    const xml = await file.async('string');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- ${path} -->\n${xml}`);
  }
  return parts.join('\n');
}

const unpacked = await unpackXlsxToXml(content);
console.log(unpacked.slice(0, 3000));
Note: content from file.text() is a UTF string — JSZip can load it but may corrupt binary. If it fails, we need to read as ArrayBuffer instead. Let's see what comes back first.

jszip.min.js:14 Uncaught Error: Can't read the data of 'the loaded zip file'. Is it in a supported JavaScript type (String, Blob, ArrayBuffer, etc) ?
    at jszip.min.js:13:35888
    at async unpackXlsxToXml (<anonymous>:19:15)
    at async <anonymous>:29:18 do browser has unzipper

9:24 AM
The issue is file.text() returns a UTF-8 string which corrupts binary. Need ArrayBuffer.

Fix the fs adapter content read — change in select:

javascript
doc.content = await file.arrayBuffer();
instead of await file.text(). Then JSZip gets raw binary directly.

But before changing adapter — browser does have native unzip via DecompressionStream but only for gzip/deflate streams, not zip archives. No native zip. JSZip is still needed, just needs ArrayBuffer not string.

give correct code

9:24 AM
javascript
// get the xlsx as ArrayBuffer via fs adapter — read handle directly
const r = await CW.run({
  target_doctype: "File",
  operation: "select",
  query: { where: { extension: "xlsx" } },
  options: { render: false }
});

// get handle from index directly — bypass text() 
const id = r.target.data[0].name;
const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
const file = await rec._handle.getFile();
const buf = await file.arrayBuffer();

// unpack
async function unpackXlsxToXml(buf) {
  const zip = await JSZip.loadAsync(buf);
  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file into xml -->'];
  for (const [path, file] of Object.entries(zip.files)) {
    if (file.dir) continue;
    const xml = await file.async('string');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- ${path} -->\n${xml}`);
  }
  return parts.join('\n');
}

const unpacked = await unpackXlsxToXml(buf);
console.log(unpacked.slice(0, 3000));
Bypasses the adapter's file.text() problem entirely — goes straight to _handle which you already have in the index.

is my unpacker ideal for AI

9:26 AM
No. Two problems for AI consumption:

1. Theme and styles are noise — xl/theme/theme1.xml is 3kb of font/color definitions. styles.xml matters only if there are date formats. AI doesn't need visual styling to understand data shape.

2. It's not resolved — AI sees <c r="B2" t="s"><v>1</v></c> and has to mentally join sharedStrings to know the value is /programs/global-entrepreneurship-week. That's extra reasoning load, and with long files it risks errors.

Ideal for AI would be:

<!-- sheet1: Лист1 -->
A1=Type | B1=insert_url | C1=external_link
A2=program | B2=/programs/startup-huddle | C2=https://...
...

<!-- sheet2: Лист2 -->
(empty)
Flat, resolved, human-readable. Sheet names included. Strings dereferenced. Styles/theme/rels dropped entirely.

So your current unpackXlsxToXml is good as a raw debug tool — you can see everything. But for feeding AI you want a second function: unpackXlsxToReadable that resolves sharedStrings and outputs a compact tabular format. Want that?

yes

9:28 AM
javascript
function unpackXlsxToReadable(buf) {
  return JSZip.loadAsync(buf).then(async zip => {

    // parse xml helper
    const parseXml = str => new DOMParser().parseFromString(str, 'application/xml');

    // load sharedStrings
    const ssFile = zip.file('xl/sharedStrings.xml');
    const strings = [];
    if (ssFile) {
      const ssXml = parseXml(await ssFile.async('string'));
      for (const si of ssXml.querySelectorAll('si')) {
        strings.push([...si.querySelectorAll('t')].map(t => t.textContent).join(''));
      }
    }

    // resolve cell value
    const resolveCell = c => {
      const v = c.querySelector('v')?.textContent ?? '';
      const f = c.querySelector('f')?.textContent;
      const t = c.getAttribute('t');
      if (f) return `=${f}`;
      if (t === 's') return strings[parseInt(v)] ?? '';
      if (t === 'b') return v === '1' ? 'TRUE' : 'FALSE';
      return v;
    };

    // col index to letter: 0→A, 1→B etc
    const colLetter = n => {
      let s = '';
      n++;
      while (n > 0) { s = String.fromCharCode(65 + (n - 1) % 26) + s; n = Math.floor((n - 1) / 26); }
      return s;
    };

    // load workbook for sheet names
    const wbXml = parseXml(await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml').async('string'));
    const sheetEls = [...wbXml.querySelectorAll('sheet')];

    const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file - resolved -->'];

    for (let si = 0; si < sheetEls.length; si++) {
      const sheetName = sheetEls[si].getAttribute('name');
      const sheetFile = zip.file(`xl/worksheets/sheet${si + 1}.xml`);
      if (!sheetFile) continue;

      const wsXml = parseXml(await sheetFile.async('string'));
      const rows = [...wsXml.querySelectorAll('row')];

      if (rows.length === 0) {
        parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si + 1}: ${sheetName} -->\n(empty)`);
        continue;
      }

      const lines = [];
      for (const row of rows) {
        const cells = [...row.querySelectorAll('c')];
        const rowObj = {};
        for (const c of cells) {
          const ref = c.getAttribute('r'); // e.g. "B3"
          const col = ref.replace(/[0-9]/g, '');
          rowObj[col] = resolveCell(c);
        }
        // find max col
        const cols = Object.keys(rowObj);
        lines.push(cols.map(col => `${col}=${rowObj[col]}`).join(' | '));
      }

      parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si + 1}: ${sheetName} -->\n${lines.join('\n')}`);
    }

    return parts.join('\n');
  });
}

is this close to ideal for AI

9:30 AM
90% there. Two small improvements for ideal:

1. Add row numbers

1: A=Type | B=insert_url | C=external_link
2: A=program | B=/programs/startup-huddle
AI can reference row 14 when flagging issues like the duplicate. Without numbers it has to count.

2. Header row as context prefix Instead of AI treating row 1 as just another row, make it explicit:

<!-- sheet1: Лист1 | columns: A=Type, B=insert_url, C=external_link -->
2: program | /programs/startup-huddle
3: program | /programs/global-entrepreneurship-week
Drop the A= prefix from data rows once headers are declared — cuts token count ~30% on wide sheets and is cleaner to read. AI already knows column mapping from the header line.

Current output is already usable — for a 3-column 18-row sheet the difference is minor. It matters more on wide sheets (10+ columns) where A=val | B=val | C=val... gets verbose and the header declaration + positional values is much more token-efficient.

Want me to update unpackXlsxToReadable with these two changes?

find 2 best practicies to present xlsx for AI that USED in top AI LLMs

9:31 AM

Searched the web
Searched the web
Two practices that actually dominate in production systems:

1. CSV/positional with explicit header declaration — used by Microsoft (Copilot in Excel patent), OpenAI, and the FinSheet-Bench benchmark. Include column headers and the first rows of data as context in the prompt, then data rows positionally without repeating column names per row. Exactly the improvement suggested earlier — declare headers once, drop A= prefix from data rows. 
uspto

2. Skeleton + type aggregation for large sheets — numerical cells sharing a format are replaced with the format name rather than exact values — "column C is dates", "column D is floats" — achieving significant compression while preserving structural understanding for the LLM. This matters when sheets are too large for context. For small sheets like yours it's overkill, but it's the standard approach in production pipelines. 
Medium

Your current output is practice #1 minus the header-declaration optimization. For your use case (small probe files feeding a code-generation prompt) you don't need #2 at all. The one change that would make it ideal: extract row 1 as the column header comment, then output data rows without column letters.

i need both, give me this funciton

9:32 AM
javascript
function unpackXlsxToReadable(buf) {
  return JSZip.loadAsync(buf).then(async zip => {

    const parseXml = str => new DOMParser().parseFromString(str, 'application/xml');

    // sharedStrings
    const ssFile = zip.file('xl/sharedStrings.xml');
    const strings = [];
    if (ssFile) {
      const ssXml = parseXml(await ssFile.async('string'));
      for (const si of ssXml.querySelectorAll('si')) {
        strings.push([...si.querySelectorAll('t')].map(t => t.textContent).join(''));
      }
    }

    // styles — collect numFmtIds that are date formats
    const dateNumFmtIds = new Set([14,15,16,17,18,19,20,21,22,45,46,47]);
    const cellXfTypes = []; // index → 'date' | 'number' | 'text'
    const stylesFile = zip.file('xl/styles.xml');
    if (stylesFile) {
      const sXml = parseXml(await stylesFile.async('string'));
      // custom numFmts
      for (const nf of sXml.querySelectorAll('numFmt')) {
        const id = parseInt(nf.getAttribute('numFmtId'));
        const code = nf.getAttribute('formatCode') || '';
        if (/[yYmMdDhHsS]/.test(code)) dateNumFmtIds.add(id);
      }
      for (const xf of sXml.querySelectorAll('cellXfs xf')) {
        const id = parseInt(xf.getAttribute('numFmtId') || '0');
        cellXfTypes.push(dateNumFmtIds.has(id) ? 'date' : 'number');
      }
    }

    const resolveCell = c => {
      const v = c.querySelector('v')?.textContent ?? '';
      const f = c.querySelector('f')?.textContent;
      const t = c.getAttribute('t');
      const s = parseInt(c.getAttribute('s') || '-1');
      if (f) return `=${f}`;
      if (t === 's') return strings[parseInt(v)] ?? '';
      if (t === 'b') return v === '1' ? 'TRUE' : 'FALSE';
      if (t === 'str' || t === 'inlineStr') return v;
      // date detection via style
      if (s >= 0 && cellXfTypes[s] === 'date') {
        const d = new Date(Math.round((parseFloat(v) - 25569) * 86400000));
        return d.toISOString().slice(0, 10);
      }
      return v;
    };

    // col ref to 0-based index: A→0, B→1, AA→26
    const colIndex = ref => {
      const col = ref.replace(/[0-9]/g, '');
      return [...col].reduce((n, c) => n * 26 + c.charCodeAt(0) - 64, 0) - 1;
    };

    // workbook sheet names
    const wbXml = parseXml(await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml').async('string'));
    const sheetEls = [...wbXml.querySelectorAll('sheet')];

    const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file - resolved -->'];

    for (let si = 0; si < sheetEls.length; si++) {
      const sheetName = sheetEls[si].getAttribute('name');
      const sheetFile = zip.file(`xl/worksheets/sheet${si + 1}.xml`);
      if (!sheetFile) continue;

      const wsXml = parseXml(await sheetFile.async('string'));
      const rows = [...wsXml.querySelectorAll('row')];

      if (rows.length === 0) {
        parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si + 1}: ${sheetName} -->\n(empty)`);
        continue;
      }

      // build 2d array
      const grid = [];
      let maxCol = 0;
      for (const row of rows) {
        const r = parseInt(row.getAttribute('r')) - 1;
        const cells = [...row.querySelectorAll('c')];
        const rowData = {};
        for (const c of cells) {
          const ci = colIndex(c.getAttribute('r'));
          rowData[ci] = resolveCell(c);
          if (ci > maxCol) maxCol = ci;
        }
        grid[r] = rowData;
      }

      // headers from row 0
      const headers = [];
      for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) {
        headers[c] = grid[0]?.[c] ?? String.fromCharCode(65 + c);
      }

      // type skeleton — per column
      const colTypes = new Array(maxCol + 1).fill(null);
      for (let r = 1; r < grid.length; r++) {
        if (!grid[r]) continue;
        for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) {
          const v = grid[r][c];
          if (v === undefined || v === '') continue;
          const t = /^\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2}$/.test(v) ? 'date'
                  : /^=/.test(v)                   ? 'formula'
                  : isNaN(v)                        ? 'text'
                  : 'number';
          if (colTypes[c] === null) colTypes[c] = t;
          else if (colTypes[c] !== t) colTypes[c] = 'mixed';
        }
      }

      const colTypeSummary = headers
        .map((h, i) => `${h}:${colTypes[i] ?? 'empty'}`)
        .join(', ');

      parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si + 1}: ${sheetName} | columns: ${colTypeSummary} -->`);

      // data rows — positional, no col letters
      const lines = [];
      for (let r = 1; r < grid.length; r++) {
        if (!grid[r]) continue;
        const vals = [];
        for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) {
          vals.push(grid[r][c] ?? '');
        }
        lines.push(`${r + 1}: ${vals.join(' | ')}`);
      }
      parts.push(lines.join('\n'));
    }

    return parts.join('\n');
  });
}
Output will look like:

<!-- sheet1: Лист1 | columns: Type:text, insert_url:text, external_link:text -->
2: program | /programs/startup-huddle | https://...
3: program | /programs/global-entrepreneurship-week | ...
Headers declared once with type skeleton, data rows positional with row numbers. Drops A= noise entirely.

9:57 AM
Good question. Let's think through it before writing anything.

What we have after CW.run select on File:

run_doc.target.data[0] has the flat record — file_name, extension, path, name. The _handle is in _fsIndex only, never in run_doc. So the handle is a side-channel lookup, not part of the data pipeline.

ArrayBuffer — store or not?

Don't store in run_doc — it's binary, potentially large, and run_doc is serialized to PocketBase as audit. Don't store in _fsIndex.rec.data either — it's redundant with the handle (you can always re-read). It's a transient processing artifact, lives only in the function scope of the pipeline step.

The real question for batch:

[file1, file2, file3]  ← select returns array
     ↓
for each: getFile() → arrayBuffer() → unpackXlsxToReadable()
     ↓
for each: update ai_content in _fsIndex
The pipeline is per-record, not per-run. So the question is where does that loop live — in the adapter, in a new CW-xlsx.js operation, or in a controller sideEffect?

My read: this is a new operation type — parse or transform — not select/update. It takes target.data (array of file records), processes each, mutates rec.data.ai_content in _fsIndex, then optionally persists. That maps cleanly to a new Adapter.fs.parse operation dispatched via CW.run with operation: 'parse'.

Does that match your thinking, or do you see it differently?

operation: 'update' but with a run_doc.script field that contains the transformation function — applied to each record in target.data (or filtered by query). The adapter executes script(record, handle) per record and writes the result back.

This is essentially map-update — select + transform + save in one operation, driven by script not hardcoded logic.

we coming back to idea of storing Run as document, and potentially FileMeta as well. advice if we can merge both. we had the dicussion on it. FileMeta as separate is good but then we need to keep mental model - File on fs+ FileMeta

10:04 AM
Yes, merging is the right call. The mental model split is the real cost — every operation needs to coordinate two records for one logical entity.

The clean solution: store ai_content (and all computed/derived fields) directly on the Run that produced them, not on File or FileMeta at all.

The Run already IS the record of "I processed file X and got result Y":

run_doc.target_doctype: "File"
run_doc.query.where: { name: "filexxx" }
run_doc.script: unpackXlsxToReadable
run_doc.target.data[0].ai_content: "<!-- unpacked..."
run_doc.status: "completed"
That Run persisted to PocketBase gives you:

what file was processed
what script ran
what the result was
when, by whom
To retrieve ai_content for a file later: query Runs where target_doctype=File, query.where.name=filexxx, operation=update, latest modified. It's a log with queryable results — no separate FileMeta needed.

The one tradeoff: retrieving current state of a file requires querying Runs not Files. But you already have CW.run for that — it's just source_doctype: "Run" lookup.

This collapses File + FileMeta + audit into one thing you already have. Does that match what you were thinking?

the merging into run has disadvantage. the FileMeta is acumulating valuable extracts, and potentially, We can even keep 1 doctype File as we have now but have dispatch into 2 adapters (not routing to fs first, but on save we can route to update db

10:07 AM
Exactly. So the architecture is:

One File doctype, two adapters in sequence — not routing, composing.

CW.run({ operation: 'update', target_doctype: 'File', ... })
     ↓
Adapter.fs.update     → writes content to disk, updates _fsIndex
     ↓ (on success)
Adapter.pb.update     → persists metadata fields (ai_content, etc.) to PocketBase `item` collection as a File record
_fsIndex stays the live handle registry. PocketBase item with doctype: "File" becomes the metadata store — name matches the same generateId("File", filename) so they're the same logical record, just split across two stores by field type:

fs adapter owns: file_name, extension, path, size, modified, content (binary/text)
pb adapter owns: ai_content, tags, notes, any other computed/derived fields
On select: fs adapter is source of truth for existence; pb record enriches with metadata if present (left join mentally).

Key advantage: FileMeta is not a separate doctype or mental model — it's just the pb-side of the same File record. name is the join key already.

One question before code: on select, do you want the adapter to auto-merge pb metadata into the fs record, or keep that explicit as a second query?

i like it. we just need to "freeze" the mental model the File in pocketbase is not snapshot of files in project directory but rather commit-like after operation like in git

10:08 AM
Perfect framing. So the mental model is:

fs = working tree. PocketBase File = commit.

A PocketBase File record only exists when something meaningful happened to that file — a parse, a transform, an AI extraction. It's not a mirror of the directory. It's a history of intentional operations, like git commits.

Consequences that fall out naturally:

select on fs adapter returns all files (working tree)
select on pb adapter returns only files that have been "committed" (have history)
update with a script = the commit act — fs does the work, pb records the result
reindex never touches pb — it only refreshes the working tree view
ai_content in pb is the committed extract, not a live field
two File records with same name in pb = two commits on same file (history, not conflict)
The name field diverges slightly here — if pb stores multiple commits per file, name can't be the join key uniquely. Options:

name = unique per file (upsert on pb, latest commit wins, no history)
name = unique per commit (append-only, query latest for current state)
Git analogy suggests append-only is more powerful. But for your use case — AI content extraction — latest-wins upsert is probably sufficient and simpler.

Which do you want?

lets note the slight issue with name (different one - i am more conserned of 2 identical filenames in different subfolders) but its ok, we have path in doc.

10:11 AM
Yes. generateId("File", filename) uses only the filename not the path, so src/utils.js and lib/utils.js would collide to the same name.

The fix is simple: hash the full path not just the filename:

generateId("File", path)  // "src/utils.js" not "utils.js"
That makes name unique per path, stable per session, and correct as the join key between fs and pb. Path is already stored in doc.path so the mental model stays clean.

Worth fixing in _recordFromHandle before building the pb commit layer — one line change, everything downstream uses name as the key correctly.

it this problem really solvable in 15 chars

10:12 AM
Good catch. generateId("File", "src/utils.js") and generateId("File", "lib/utils.js") — if generateId hashes the whole string into 15 chars there will eventually be collisions. 15 chars of nanoid is ~89 bits of randomness which is fine for random IDs, but if it's a deterministic hash of a short string the space is the same but the collision risk is real for similar paths.

What does your generateId actually do — random nanoid with a prefix, or hash-based?

// ============================================================
// CW-run.js — refactored
// Signal format: "dim.from_to" — e.g. "0.0_1", "1.0_1"
// FSM pure helpers in CW-utils.js
// target.data[0] is single source of truth
// input is cleared after _mergeInput — all reads from target
// ============================================================

//const CW = globalThis.CW;



// ============================================================
// RESOLVER
// ============================================================

CW._resolveAll = function (op) {
  const cfg = CW._config;

  op.operation =
    cfg.operationAliases?.[op.operation?.toLowerCase()] || op.operation;

  const dtMap = cfg.doctypeAliases || {};
  op.source_doctype = op.source_doctype
    ? dtMap[op.source_doctype.toLowerCase()] || op.source_doctype
    : null;
  op.target_doctype = op.target_doctype
    ? dtMap[op.target_doctype.toLowerCase()] || op.target_doctype
    : null;

  const opConfig    = cfg.operations?.[op.operation] || {};
  /* const adapterType = opConfig.adapterType || 'db';
  op.adapter        = cfg.adapters?.defaults?.[adapterType] || cfg.adapters?.defaults?.db; */

  const adapterType = opConfig.adapterType || 'db';
//const doctypeOverride = cfg.adapters?.doctypeAdapters?.[run_doc.target_doctype];

const doctypeOverride = cfg.adapters?.doctypeAdapters?.[op.target_doctype];
op.adapter = doctypeOverride 
  || cfg.adapters?.defaults?.[adapterType] 
  || cfg.adapters?.defaults?.db;

  const view       = cfg.operationToView?.[op.operation] ?? null;
  const viewConfig = cfg.views?.[view?.toLowerCase()] || {};
  op.view          = 'view' in op ? op.view : view;

  // skip component/container resolution for child runs
if (op.parent_run_id && op.options?.render === false) {
  if (!('component' in op)) op.component = null;
  if (!('container' in op)) op.container = null;
  return;
}

  const resolvedView = op.view || view;
  if (!('component' in op) || !('container' in op)) {
    let resolved = null;
    if (resolvedView && CW._resolveViewComponent) {
      resolved = CW._resolveViewComponent(op.target_doctype, resolvedView, op.container);
    }
    if (resolved && typeof resolved === 'object') {
      if (!('component' in op)) op.component = resolved.component ?? null;
      if (!('container' in op)) op.container = resolved.container ?? viewConfig.container ?? null;
    } else {
      if (!('component' in op)) op.component = (typeof resolved === 'string' ? resolved : null) ?? viewConfig.component ?? null;
      if (!('container' in op)) op.container = viewConfig.container ?? null;
    }
  }
};

// ============================================================
// RESOLVE INPUT — meta channel: input['.field'] → run_doc.field
// ============================================================

CW._resolveInput = function (run_doc) {
  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(run_doc.input)) {
    if (key.startsWith('.')) {
      run_doc[key.slice(1)] = value;
      delete run_doc.input[key];
    }
  }
};

// ============================================================
// MERGE INPUT → target.data[0]
// Everything including virtual and _state
// ============================================================

CW._mergeInput = function (run_doc) {
  if (!run_doc.target) run_doc.target = { data: [{}] };
  if (!run_doc.target.data) run_doc.target.data = [{}];
  if (!run_doc.target.data[0]) run_doc.target.data[0] = {};

  const doc = run_doc.target.data[0];

  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(run_doc.input)) {
    if (k === '_state') continue;
    doc[k] = v;
  }

  if (run_doc.input._state && typeof run_doc.input._state === 'object') {
    if (!doc._state) doc._state = {};
    const inputState  = run_doc.input._state;
    const targetState = doc._state;

    // preserve history — only overwrite the exact incoming signal keys
    //for (const sig of Object.keys(inputState)) {
    //  delete targetState[sig];
    //}
    Object.assign(targetState, inputState);
  }
};

// ============================================================
// CLEAR INPUT — empty input after merge, preserve _state shape
// ============================================================

CW._clearInput = function (run_doc) {
  run_doc.input = { _state: {} };
};

// ============================================================
// STRIP VIRTUAL — remove virtual fields from target before persist
// ============================================================

CW._stripVirtual = function (run_doc) {
  const schema = CW.Schema?.[run_doc.target_doctype];
  const doc    = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!schema?.fields || !doc) return;
  schema.fields.filter(f => f.virtual).forEach(f => delete doc[f.fieldname]);
};

// ============================================================
// _execTransition — fire sideEffects + sync docstatus + view switch
// ============================================================

CW._execTransition = async function (run_doc, dim, key) {
  const doctype  = run_doc.target_doctype;
  const stateDef = CW._getStateDef(doctype);
  const dimDef   = stateDef[dim];
  if (!dimDef) return;

  // collect and fire sideEffects
  const effects = Object.entries(dimDef.sideEffects || {}).filter(
    ([k]) => k === key || k.startsWith(key + '.'),
  );

  for (const [effectKey, fn] of effects) {
    if (effectKey === key) {
      if (typeof fn === 'function') {
        await fn(run_doc);
      } else if (typeof fn === 'string') {
        // string path — resolve from globalThis e.g. "Adapter.pocketbase.signUp"
        const path   = fn.split('.');
        let resolved = globalThis;
        for (const p of path) resolved = resolved?.[p];
        if (typeof resolved === 'function') await resolved(run_doc);
        else console.warn('[CW] Effect not found:', fn);
      }
    } else {
      const path   = effectKey.slice(key.length + 1).split('.');
      let target   = globalThis;
      for (const p of path) target = target?.[p];
      if (typeof target === 'function') await target(run_doc);
      else console.warn('[CW] Adapter effect not found:', effectKey.slice(key.length + 1));
    }
  }

  // sync docstatus for dim 0 → target.data[0]
  const to  = parseInt(key.split('_')[1]);
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (doc && String(dim) === '0') {
    doc.docstatus = to;
  }

  // view switch after transition
  if (run_doc.container && dimDef.views?.[String(to)]) {
    const view      = dimDef.views[String(to)];
    const resolved  = CW._resolveViewComponent(doctype, view, run_doc.container);
    const component = resolved?.component ?? (typeof resolved === 'string' ? resolved : null);
    const container = run_doc.container || resolved?.container || CW._config.views?.[view]?.container;
    if (component) {
      await run_doc.child({
        operation:      'select',
        target_doctype: doctype,
        query:          { where: { name: run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name || run_doc.query?.where?.name } },
        view, component, container,
        options:        { render: true },
        source_field:   '_state',   // ← add
      });
    }
  }
};

// ============================================================
// HANDLE SIGNAL
// Reads signal from target.data[0]._state
// All reads/writes go to target.data[0]
// ============================================================

CW._handleSignal = async function (run_doc) {
  const _savedInternal = run_doc.options?.internal;
  if (!run_doc.options) run_doc.options = {};
  run_doc.options.internal = true;

  const signal   = run_doc._signal;
  const doctype  = run_doc.target_doctype;
  const schema   = CW.Schema?.[doctype];
  //const db       = CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;  //NEVER used
  const doc      = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};

  const stateDef = CW._getStateDef(doctype);

const _failSignal = (err, dim, fromVal) => {
  run_doc.error = err;
  if (doc._state && dim !== undefined) {
    doc._state[signal] = '-1';
    doc._state[dim] = fromVal;
  }
  run_doc.options.internal = _savedInternal;
};

  let matched = false;

  for (const [dim, dimDef] of Object.entries(stateDef)) {
    if (!signal.startsWith(dim + '.')) continue;
    const key = signal.slice(dim.length + 1);

    if (dimDef.sideEffects?.[key] === undefined && dimDef.labels?.[key] === undefined) continue;

    const currentVal = CW._getDimValue(doc, dim, dimDef);
    const fromVal    = parseInt(key.split('_')[0]);
    const toVal      = parseInt(key.split('_')[1]);

    if (!isNaN(fromVal) && !isNaN(toVal)) {
      const validTos = dimDef.transitions?.[String(currentVal)] || [];
      if (fromVal !== currentVal || !validTos.includes(toVal)) {
        _failSignal(`Transition ${key} not allowed from current state ${currentVal} (dim ${dim})`);
        return;
      }
    }

    const requires  = dimDef.requires?.[key] || {};
    const reqPassed = Object.entries(requires).every(
      ([k, v]) => Number(schema?.[k] ?? 0) === Number(v),
    );
    if (!reqPassed) {
      _failSignal(`${signal} not allowed for this doctype`);
      return;
    }

    const rule = dimDef.rules?.[key];
    if (typeof rule === 'function' && !rule(run_doc)) {
      _failSignal(`${signal} rule not satisfied`);
      return;
    }

    try {
      await CW._execTransition(run_doc, dim, key);

      // preserve full history — mark signal success
      if (!doc._state) doc._state = {};
      doc._state[signal] = '1';
      doc._state[dim] = toVal;   // ← ADDed THIS LINE

      // also mark in input._state so _preflight picks it up for DB write
      run_doc.input._state[signal] = '1';

      run_doc.operation = doc.name ? 'update' : 'create';
      if (run_doc.operation === 'update') {
        await CW._handlers.update(run_doc);
      } else {
        await CW._handlers.create(run_doc);
      }

    } catch (e) {
      _failSignal(e.message);
    }

    matched = true;
    break;
  }

  if (!matched) {
    if (signal === 'save') {
      run_doc.operation = doc.name ? 'update' : 'create';
      await CW._handlers[run_doc.operation](run_doc);

    } else if (signal === 'submit') {
      doc.docstatus    = 1;
      run_doc.operation = 'update';
      await CW._handlers.update(run_doc);

    } else if (signal === 'cancel') {
      doc.docstatus    = 2;
      run_doc.operation = 'update';
      await CW._handlers.update(run_doc);

    } else if (signal === 'amend') {
      if ((doc.docstatus ?? 0) !== 2) {
        _failSignal('amend only allowed on cancelled records (docstatus=2)');
        return;
      }
      const skipAmend = new Set(['name','id','created','modified','modified_by','_state','docstatus','amended_from']);
      const newDoc = {};
      for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(doc)) {
        if (!skipAmend.has(k)) newDoc[k] = v;
      }
      newDoc.amended_from = doc.name;
      newDoc.docstatus    = 0;
      run_doc.target      = { data: [newDoc] };
      run_doc.operation   = 'create';
      await CW._handlers.create(run_doc);

    } else {
      _failSignal(`Unknown signal: ${signal}`);
    }
  }

  run_doc.options.internal = _savedInternal;

  if (!run_doc.error) {
    if (run_doc.operation === 'create' && run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name) {
      run_doc.query = Object.assign({}, run_doc.query, {
        where: { name: run_doc.target.data[0].name },
      });
    }
  }
};

// ============================================================
// CW._expand 
// ============================================================

CW._getChildRun = function (run_doc, fieldname) {
  if (!fieldname) return null;
  return run_doc.child_run_ids
    .map(id => CW.runs[id])
    .find(r => r?.source_field === fieldname) || null;
};


//=============================================================


CW._expand = async function (run_doc, fieldname) {
  const schema  = CW.Schema?.[run_doc.target_doctype];
  const doc     = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  const docName = doc?.name;
  if (!schema || !docName) return;

  const fields = fieldname
    ? schema.fields?.filter(f => f.fieldname === fieldname)
    : schema.fields?.filter(f =>
        f.fieldtype === 'Table'              ||
        f.fieldtype === 'Relationship Panel' ||
        f.fieldtype === 'Link'               ||
        f.fieldtype === 'ChildRun'
      );

  const promises = [];
  for (const field of fields || []) {
    const exists = run_doc.child_run_ids
      .some(id => CW.runs[id]?.source_field === field.fieldname);
    if (exists) continue;

    if (field.fieldtype === 'ChildRun') {
      promises.push(run_doc.child({
        ...field.run_args,
        operation:    field.run_args?.operation || 'select',
        query:        CW._resolveQuery(run_doc, field.fieldname),
        source_field: field.fieldname,
        options:      { render: false },
        component:    null,
        container:    null,
      }));
      continue;
    }

    if (field.fieldtype === 'Link') {
      const val = doc[field.fieldname];
      if (!val) continue;
      promises.push(run_doc.child({
        operation:      'select',
        target_doctype: field.options,
        query:          { where: { name: val } },
        source_field:   field.fieldname,
        options:        { render: false },
        view:           'list',
        component:      null,
        container:      null,
      }));
      continue;
    }

    promises.push(run_doc.child({
      operation:      'select',
      target_doctype: field.options,
      query:          { where: { parent: docName } },
      source_field:   field.fieldname,
      options:        { render: false },
      view:           'list',
      component:      null,
      container:      null,
    }));
  }

  await Promise.all(promises);
};

// ============================================================
// CONTROLLER
// ============================================================

CW.controller = async function (run_doc) {
  run_doc.status = 'running';
  run_doc.error  = null;

  try {
    // 1. meta channel — input['.field'] → run_doc.field
    CW._resolveInput(run_doc);

if (
  (run_doc.operation === 'update' || run_doc.operation === 'delete') &&
  !run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name
) {
  //await globalThis.Adapter[CW._config.adapters.defaults.db].select(run_doc)

   await CW._handlers.select(run_doc);
}

    await CW._logChanges(run_doc)  // ← before merge

    // 2. merge all input → target.data[0] (including virtual + _state)
    CW._mergeInput(run_doc);

    // 3. clear input — everything is now in target.data[0]
    CW._clearInput(run_doc);

    const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};

    // 4. dispatch: signal or data or operation
    const signal = Object.entries(doc._state || {}).find(([,v]) => v === '');

    if (signal) {
      run_doc._signal = signal[0];
      await CW._handleSignal(run_doc);
    } else {
      const opConfig = CW._config.operations?.[run_doc.operation] || {};
      if (opConfig.type === 'read' || opConfig.type === 'auth') {
        await CW._handlers[run_doc.operation]?.(run_doc);
      } else {
        // data change — create or update
        const schema   = CW.Schema?.[run_doc.target_doctype];
        const autosave = schema?._autosave ?? 1;
        if (autosave !== 0) {
          run_doc.operation = doc.name ? 'update' : 'create';
          await CW._handlers[run_doc.operation](run_doc);
          if (!run_doc.error && run_doc.operation === 'create' && run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name) {
            run_doc.query = Object.assign({}, run_doc.query, {
              where: { name: run_doc.target.data[0].name },
            });
          }
        }
      }
    }

    run_doc.status  = run_doc.error ? 'failed' : 'completed';
    run_doc.success = !run_doc.error;

  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = {
      message: err.message,
      code:    `${run_doc.operation?.toUpperCase()}_FAILED`,
    };
    run_doc.status  = 'failed';
    run_doc.success = false;
  }

  run_doc.modified = Date.now();
  if (CW._updateFromRun) CW._updateFromRun(run_doc);
  if (CW._render && run_doc.options?.render === true) CW._render(run_doc);
};

// ============================================================
// RUN FACTORY
// ============================================================

CW.run = async function (op) {
  CW._resolveAll(op);

  const run_doc = {
    doctype:            'Run',
    name:               generateId('Run'),
    creation:           Date.now(),
    modified:           Date.now(),
    owner:              op.owner || 'system',
    modified_by:        op.owner || 'system',
    docstatus:          0,

    operation:          op.operation,
    operation_original: op.operation,
    source_doctype:     op.source_doctype,

    search:             op.search || '',
    source_field:       op.source_field ?? null,

    target_doctype:     op.target_doctype,
    adapter:            op.adapter,

    view:               op.view,
    component:          op.component,
    container:          op.container,
    context:            op.context || {},  //DO NOT USE IT

    query:              op.query  || {},
    target:             op.target || null,
    input:              op.input  || {},

    status:             'pending',
    success:            false,
    error:              null,

    parent_run_id:      op.parent_run_id || null,
    child_run_ids:      [],
    options:            op.options || {},
    user: op.user ?? {
      name:     globalThis.pb?.authStore?.model?.id     ?? null,
      email:    globalThis.pb?.authStore?.model?.email  ?? null,
      token:    globalThis.pb?.authStore?.token         ?? null,
      verified: globalThis.pb?.authStore?.model?.verified ?? false,
    },
  };

  run_doc.child = async function (childOp) {
    childOp.parent_run_id = run_doc.name;
    childOp.user          = childOp.user ?? run_doc.user;
    const child           = await CW.run(childOp);
    if (!run_doc.child_run_ids.includes(child.name)) {
      run_doc.child_run_ids.push(child.name);
    }
    return child;
  };

  CW.runs[run_doc.name] = run_doc;
  if (CW._updateFromRun) CW._updateFromRun(run_doc);
  await CW.controller(run_doc);
  return run_doc;
};

// ============================================================
// PREFLIGHT
// Operates on target.data[0] — not input
// ============================================================

CW._preflight = function (run_doc) {
  const operation = run_doc.operation;
  const schema = CW.Schema?.[run_doc.target_doctype];
  const doc    = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc) return;

  if (operation === 'create') {
    // reqd validation
    if (schema?.fields) {
      const missing = schema.fields
        .filter(f =>
          f.reqd &&
          f.fieldtype !== 'Table' &&
          evaluateDependsOn(f.depends_on, doc, run_doc) &&
          (doc[f.fieldname] === undefined || doc[f.fieldname] === null || doc[f.fieldname] === ''),
        )
        .map(f => f.label || f.fieldname);
      if (missing.length) {
        run_doc.error = `Required: ${missing.join(', ')}`;
        return;
      }
    }

    // apply defaults
    if (schema?.fields) {
      for (const f of schema.fields) {
        if (f.default !== undefined && doc[f.fieldname] === undefined) {
          doc[f.fieldname] = f.default;
        }
      }
    }

    // initialize _state
    if (!doc._state) doc._state = {};

  }

  if (operation === 'update') {   //was if (operation === 'update'
    // reqd validation against target.data[0] (already merged)
    if (schema?.fields) {
      const missing = schema.fields
        .filter(f =>
          f.reqd &&
           !f.virtual &&
          f.fieldtype !== 'Table' &&
          evaluateDependsOn(f.depends_on, doc, run_doc) &&
          (doc[f.fieldname] === undefined || doc[f.fieldname] === null || doc[f.fieldname] === ''),
        )
        .map(f => f.label || f.fieldname);
      if (missing.length) {
        run_doc.error = `Required: ${missing.join(', ')}`;
        return;
      }
    }
  }

  // JSON stringify Code fields
  if (schema?.fields) {
    for (const f of schema.fields) {
      if (
        f.fieldtype === 'Code' &&
        f.options   === 'JSON' &&
        typeof doc[f.fieldname] === 'object'
      ) {
        if (f.fieldname === '_state') continue;
        doc[f.fieldname] = JSON.stringify(doc[f.fieldname]);
      }
    }
  }

  // systemFields — operate on target.data[0] via run_doc
  for (const sf of CW._config.systemFields || []) {
    if (sf.onWrite)                    sf.onWrite(run_doc);
    if (sf.onCreate && operation === 'create') sf.onCreate(run_doc);
  }
};

// ============================================================
// HANDLERS
// ============================================================

CW._handlers = {

  select: async function (run_doc) {
    /*const db = CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
    await globalThis.Adapter[db].select(run_doc);*/

    await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].select(run_doc); //insetad


    if (run_doc.error || !run_doc.target?.data) return;

    const schema     = CW.Schema?.[run_doc.target_doctype ?? run_doc.source_doctype];
    const activeView = run_doc.view || run_doc.query?.view || 'list';
    const sel        = run_doc.query?.select;

    if (schema && !sel) {
      const shouldFilter = activeView === 'list' || activeView === 'card';
      if (shouldFilter) {
        const viewFields   = schema.fields.filter(f => f.in_list_view).map(f => f.fieldname);
        const titleField   = schema.title_field ? [schema.title_field] : [];
        //const systemFields = (CW._config.systemFields || []).filter(sf => sf.fetch).map(sf => sf.name);
        //const fields       = [...new Set([...systemFields, ...titleField, ...viewFields])];
        const fields     = [...new Set([...titleField, ...viewFields])];
        run_doc.target.data = run_doc.target.data.map(item => {
          const filtered = {};
          fields.forEach(f => { if (f in item) filtered[f] = item[f]; });
          return filtered;
        });
      }
    } else if (sel && Array.isArray(sel)) {
      const titleField   = schema?.title_field ? [schema.title_field] : [];
      const systemFields = CW.defaultFields || [];
      const allFields    = [...new Set([...systemFields, ...titleField, ...sel])];
      run_doc.target.data = run_doc.target.data.map(item => {
        const filtered = {};
        allFields.forEach(f => { if (f in item) filtered[f] = item[f]; });
        return filtered;
      });
    }

    // expand child fields for form view — after data is ready
  if (run_doc.view === 'form' && run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name) {
    await CW._expand(run_doc);
  }
  },

  create: async function (run_doc) {
    CW._preflight(run_doc);
    if (run_doc.error) return;
    CW._stripVirtual(run_doc);  // strip virtual after validation, before DB write
    /* const db = CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
    await globalThis.Adapter[db].create(run_doc); */
    await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].create(run_doc);
  },

  update: async function (run_doc) {
    //const db  = CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
    const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
    const name = doc?.name || run_doc.query?.where?.name;

    if (!name) {
      run_doc.error = 'Update requires a record name';
      return;
    }
    if (!run_doc.query?.where?.name) {
      run_doc.query = Object.assign({}, run_doc.query, { where: { name } });
    }

    const editable = (doc?.docstatus ?? 0) === 0;
    if (!editable && !run_doc.options?.internal) return;

    CW._preflight(run_doc);
    if (run_doc.error) return;
    CW._stripVirtual(run_doc);  // strip virtual after validation, before DB write
    //await globalThis.Adapter[db].update(run_doc);

    await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].update(run_doc);
  },

  delete: async function (run_doc) {
    if (run_doc.target?.data?.[0]) run_doc.target.data[0].docstatus = 2;
    await CW._handlers.update(run_doc);
  },

};

console.log('✅ CW-run.js loaded (signal format: dim.from_to e.g. 0.0_1, 1.0_1)');

Yes, very solvable without changing much. The key is here:

javascript
await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].update(run_doc);
After that line succeeds, you just add:

javascript
if (!run_doc.error && run_doc.adapter === 'fs') {
  await globalThis.Adapter['pocketbase'].update(run_doc);
}
Same run_doc, same target.data[0] — pb adapter gets the already-merged doc with ai_content included. No new fields, no new operations, no schema changes.

The only thing pb adapter needs is that the record has a name (which generateId("File", path) already provides) and target_doctype: "File" so it routes to the item collection correctly.

One question before touching anything: the pb update will try to write ALL fields in target.data[0] including content (potentially large binary). Do you want to strip content before the pb write, keeping pb as metadata-only store?

10:18 AM
Yes. Instead of hardcoding the fs → pb sequence in the handler, run_doc.adapter becomes an array:

javascript
adapter: ['fs', 'pocketbase']
Handler iterates:

javascript
for (const adapter of [].concat(run_doc.adapter)) {
  await globalThis.Adapter[adapter][run_doc.operation](run_doc);
  if (run_doc.error) break;
}
That's the only change to CW-run.js. Everything else stays identical.

Config drives it — doctypeAdapters for File becomes:

javascript
doctypeAdapters: {
  File: ['fs', 'pocketbase']
}
Select would naturally take first adapter only (or merge results — but that's a separate question). For write operations the chain makes sense. For select you'd want adapter[0] as source of truth.

So the real question is: same chain behavior for all operations, or per-operation adapter config?

javascript
doctypeAdapters: {
  File: {
    select: 'fs',
    update: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
    create: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
    delete: ['fs', 'pocketbase']
  }
}
That's slightly more config but gives precise control. Worth it?

This already assigns the whole config object to op.adapter. Then in the handler, one helper resolves it:

javascript
CW._getAdapters = function(run_doc) {
  const a = run_doc.adapter;
  if (!a) return [CW._config.adapters.defaults.db];
  if (typeof a === 'string') return [a];
  if (Array.isArray(a)) return a;
  // per-operation map
  const resolved = a[run_doc.operation] || a['default'] || CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
  return [].concat(resolved);
};
Then every handler becomes:

javascript
for (const adapter of CW._getAdapters(run_doc)) {
  await globalThis.Adapter[adapter][run_doc.operation](run_doc);
  if (run_doc.error) break;
}
Three places change in CW-run.js: select, create, update handlers — each replaces one Adapter[run_doc.adapter].operation(run_doc) call with the loop. _resolveAll stays untouched. Config gains per-operation adapter map for File.

10:28 AM
Looking at the chain:

1. _resolveAll — does it break? doctypeAdapters.File is now an object {select: 'fs', update: [...]} not a string. op.adapter gets assigned the whole object. _resolveAll just assigns, doesn't read it. ✅ no break.

2. run_doc.adapter flows through — does it break? CW.run factory copies op.adapter to run_doc.adapter. Still just assignment. ✅ no break.

3. Current handler call — does it break?

javascript
await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].update(run_doc)
run_doc.adapter is now an object. Adapter[{...}] → undefined. .update → TypeError. ❌ this breaks today without _getAdapters.

4. Select with adapter: {select: 'fs', ...} — breaks same way. ❌

Conclusion: _resolveAll and the factory are safe. The only breakage is the three handler lines that do Adapter[run_doc.adapter].operation() directly. Nothing else touches run_doc.adapter.

So the minimal safe sequence is: add _getAdapters first, then update config. In that order nothing breaks mid-deploy. Agree?

10:30 AM
Currently in the handler:

javascript
await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].update(run_doc)
run_doc.adapter is expected to be a string like "pocketbase" or "fs". JavaScript uses it as the key to look up Adapter["pocketbase"] which returns the adapter object.

If you put the per-operation config in doctypeAdapters:

javascript
File: { select: 'fs', update: ['fs', 'pocketbase'] }
Then run_doc.adapter becomes that whole object {select: 'fs', update: [...]}. Now:

javascript
Adapter[{select: 'fs', update: [...]}]
JavaScript coerces the object key to a string → Adapter["[object Object]"] → undefined. Then .update(run_doc) on undefined → TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined.

Same happens in select handler — same line pattern, same crash.

Nothing is wrong with the config idea — the problem is purely that the three handler lines assume run_doc.adapter is always a string. They need _getAdapters sitting between them and run_doc.adapter before the config change goes in. That's the only required ordering.

is our approach to naming is ideal await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter]

10:33 AM
No. globalThis.Adapter is a flat registry — Adapter.fs, Adapter.pocketbase. But the name Adapter implies a single thing, not a registry of many.

Better names used in real frameworks:

Adapters (plural) — simple, honest
CW.adapters — namespaced, consistent with CW.runs, CW.Schema
CW.Adapter — your current pattern but on CW not globalThis
The globalThis part is the bigger issue. Everything else in CW lives on CW.* — CW.runs, CW.Schema, CW.controller. But adapters live on globalThis.Adapter as a separate global. That's an inconsistency.

The clean version:

javascript
await CW.adapters[adapterName][run_doc.operation](run_doc)
With registration:

javascript
CW.adapters = CW.adapters || {};
CW.adapters.fs = { select, create, update, delete: del, reindex };
But this is a naming/namespace cleanup — not a blocker for the current work. Worth noting for when you freeze the architecture. Do you want to keep globalThis.Adapter for now and rename in one pass later?

adain if we keep globalThis.Adapter what final changes you propose

10:34 AM
Keep globalThis.Adapter, minimal changes only:

1. Rename to globalThis.Adapters (plural) — one find/replace across all files, honest about being a registry.

2. Add CW._getAdapters(run_doc) — the helper that resolves string/array/object to []string. One new function in CW-run.js.

3. Replace 3 handler lines — select, create, update each replace:

javascript
await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].operation(run_doc)
with:

javascript
for (const a of CW._getAdapters(run_doc)) {
  await globalThis.Adapters[a][run_doc.operation](run_doc);
  if (run_doc.error) break;
}
4. Update self-register in each adapter file — last line changes from:

javascript
globalThis.Adapter.fs = {...}
to:

javascript
globalThis.Adapters = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.fs = {...}
That's it. 4 changes, no logic touched, fully backward compatible if you do them together.

  689    },
