  691    update: async function (run_doc) {
  692      //const db  = CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
  693      const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  694      const name = doc?.name || run_doc.query?.where?.name;
  695  
  696      if (!name) {
  697        run_doc.error = 'Update requires a record name';
  698        return;

  700      if (!run_doc.query?.where?.name) {
  701        run_doc.query = Object.assign({}, run_doc.query, { where: { name } });
  702      }
  703  
  704      const editable = (doc?.docstatus ?? 0) === 0;
  705      if (!editable && !run_doc.options?.internal) return;
  706  
  707      CW._preflight(run_doc);
  708      if (run_doc.error) return;
  709      CW._stripVirtual(run_doc);  // strip virtual after validation, before DB write
  710:     //await globalThis.Adapter[db].update(run_doc);
  711  
  712:     await globalThis.Adapter[run_doc.adapter].update(run_doc);
  713    },
  714  
  715    delete: async function (run_doc) {
  716      if (run_doc.target?.data?.[0]) run_doc.target.data[0].docstatus = 2;
  717      await CW._handlers.update(run_doc);
  718    },
  719  
  720  };

again what strategic advantage i get after this

10:42 AM
One config line drives the entire persistence strategy for any doctype:

javascript
File: {
  select: 'fs',
  update: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
  create: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
  delete: 'fs'
}
No code changes for new storage patterns — only config. Concrete advantages:

1. Future adapters are free — S3, IndexedDB, REST API, local SQLite. Wire them in config, zero handler changes.

2. Sync patterns declarable — ['fs', 'pocketbase'] is write-through. Swap order to ['pocketbase', 'fs'] for write-back. Add a cache adapter in position 0 for read-through. All config.

3. Per-operation control — select: 'fs' means reads never hit PocketBase for File. delete: 'fs' means deletes don't touch pb (soft commit model). Surgical.

4. Every doctype can have its own strategy — Run stays pocketbase only. File is fs + pocketbase. A future Cache doctype could be indexeddb only. Single mental model covers all cases.

The cost is 6 line renames + 1 helper function. The gain is the adapter layer becomes a first-class routing system instead of a hardcoded string lookup.

lets start with refactorng del to delete - this was bad naming in fs adapter

10:43 AM
WILL CHANGE: CW-adapter-fs.js — rename del to delete_ (can't use reserved word delete as function name, so delete_) and update self-register.

WILL NOT TOUCH: everything else.

Two changes:

javascript
// line: async function del(run_doc)
async function delete_(run_doc) {
javascript
// line: globalThis.Adapter.fs = { init, select, create, update, delete: del, reindex }
globalThis.Adapter.fs = { init, select, create, update, delete: delete_, reindex };
delete: key stays as delete in the registry — only the internal function name changes from del to delete_. Callers use Adapter.fs.delete(run_doc) which stays the same. Proceed?

why delete_

10:44 AM
Because delete is a reserved word in JavaScript — you can't use it as a function declaration name:

javascript
async function delete(run_doc) {} // SyntaxError
But in the registry key it's fine:

javascript
{ delete: delete_ }  // key is just a string
Same reason the pb adapter uses del currently. Options:

delete_ — common convention for reserved word conflicts
del — what pb adapter already uses, consistent
deleteRecord — verbose but clear
Since pb adapter already uses del and you're trying to be consistent across adapters — del is actually the better choice. Keep both adapters using del internally, expose as delete: in the registry. Proceed with del?

lets keep del then. whats first to refactor

adapters: {
    // Default adapter per category
    defaults: {
      db: "pocketbase",
      auth: "auth",
      storage: null, // Future
      email: null, // Future
    },
    payloadAdapters: {
      Request: "auth",
      Object: null, //was "run-builder"
      Run: null,
    },


      // doctype → adapter name mapping
  // if target_doctype matches, use this adapter instead of db
  doctypeAdapters: {
    File:      "fs",
    GitCommit: "git",
    GitBranch: "git",
    GitDiff:   "git",
  },
  

    // Adapter registry (defines what's available)
    registry: {
      // ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────
      // DATABASE ADAPTERS
      // ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────
      pocketbase: {
        type: "db",
        name: "PocketBase",

// ============================================================
// _getAdapters — resolves adapter config to string array
// ============================================================

CW._getAdapters = function(run_doc) {
  const a = run_doc.adapter;
  if (!a) return [CW._config.adapters.defaults.db];
  if (typeof a === 'string') return [a];
  if (Array.isArray(a)) return a;
  const resolved = a[run_doc.operation] || a['default'] || CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
  return [].concat(resolved);
};

CW._handlers = {

  select: async function (run_doc) {
    /*const db = CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
    await globalThis.Adapters[db].select(run_doc);*/

    await globalThis.Adapters[run_doc.adapter].select(run_doc); //insetad


    if (run_doc.error || !run_doc.target?.data) return;

    const schema     = CW.Schema?.[run_doc.target_doctype ?? run_doc.source_doctype];
    const activeView = run_doc.view || run_doc.query?.view || 'list';
    const sel        = run_doc.query?.select;

    if (schema && !sel) {
      const shouldFilter = activeView === 'list' || activeView === 'card';
      if (shouldFilter) {
        const viewFields   = schema.fields.filter(f => f.in_list_view).map(f => f.fieldname);
        const titleField   = schema.title_field ? [schema.title_field] : [];
        //const systemFields = (CW._config.systemFields || []).filter(sf => sf.fetch).map(sf => sf.name);
        //const fields       = [...new Set([...systemFields, ...titleField, ...viewFields])];

          const filtered = {};
          fields.forEach(f => { if (f in item) filtered[f] = item[f]; });
          return filtered;
        });
      }
    } else if (sel && Array.isArray(sel)) {
      const titleField   = schema?.title_field ? [schema.title_field] : [];
      const systemFields = CW.defaultFields || [];
      const allFields    = [...new Set([...systemFields, ...titleField, ...sel])];
      run_doc.target.data = run_doc.target.data.map(item => {
        const filtered = {};
        allFields.forEach(f => { if (f in item) filtered[f] = item[f]; });
        return filtered;
      });
    }

    // expand child fields for form view — after data is ready
  if (run_doc.view === 'form' && run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name) {
    await CW._expand(run_doc);
  }
  },

    await globalThis.Adapters[db].create(run_doc); */
    await globalThis.Adapters[run_doc.adapter].create(run_doc);

    if (!name) {
      run_doc.error = 'Update requires a record name';
      return;
    }
    if (!run_doc.query?.where?.name) {
      run_doc.query = Object.assign({}, run_doc.query, { where: { name } });
    }

    const editable = (doc?.docstatus ?? 0) === 0;
    if (!editable && !run_doc.options?.internal) return;

    CW._preflight(run_doc);
    if (run_doc.error) return;
    CW._stripVirtual(run_doc);  // strip virtual after validation, before DB write
    //await globalThis.Adapters[db].update(run_doc);

  },

  delete: async function (run_doc) {

    await CW._handlers.update(run_doc);
  },

The error is from the fs adapter, not pb. "State cached in an interface object" — this is the File System Access API saying the FileSystemFileHandle is stale after reindex rebuilt _fsIndex, creating new handle entries.

The issue: reindex replaces the entire _fsIndex with a new Map, but the name (id) is generated by generateId("File", filename) which should be stable. Let me check — after reindex, does the same file get the same name?

The real problem is likely that reindex is called, new handles are in _fsIndex, but then the update uses the name from the pre-reindex select. The handle stored under that name in the new index may be a different object.

lets define conditions first as this is not 100% solvable issue (as we might have same name different path files, as path unforttunately is relative for different FileAPI sessions. so we can not 100% "anchor" file but we will try with 99% prob now

11:08 AM
Good framing. Conditions for 99% stable id:

What we have per file that's stable across sessions:

file_name — stable
path — relative from picked root, stable if same root picked
size — changes on edit
lastModified — changes on edit
extension — stable
What changes:

the root itself — user could pick a different parent folder
lastModified / size — change on any write
99% anchor = file_name + path — stable as long as same root is picked, which is the normal case (IDB restores the same handle). Collisions only if genuinely identical relative paths in different roots, which is an edge case worth accepting.

So generateId("File", path) where path is the full relative path like src/utils.js — not just filename. That's the fix.

One line change in _recordFromHandle:

javascript
const id = generateId("File", path);  // was generateId("File", handle.name)
But this only works if generateId is deterministic — not random. Is it a hash or nanoid?

11:11 AM
Right. generateId prefix + 15 char id — if it's hashing the input into 15 chars, long paths will collide with other long paths that share the same hash prefix.

i think the closest is userid that hasing email in unique string 

const SINGLE_DOCTYPES = new Set([
  "Role",
  "Country",
  "Currency",
  "Department",
  "Designation",
  "Territory",
  "UOM",
  "UOM Category",
  "Item Group",
  "Customer Group",
  "Supplier Group",
  "Tax Category",
  "Mode of Payment",
  "Terms and Conditions",
  "Print Heading",
  "Brand",
  "Item Attribute",
  "Warehouse Type",
  "Industry Type",
  "Market Segment",
  "Sales Stage",
  "Employee Group",
  "Holiday List",
  "Workstation Type",
  "Activity Type",
  "Project Type",
  "Schema",
  "Task Type",
  "Issue Type",
  "Party Type",
]);

const EMAIL_KEYED = {
  User: "user",
  UserPublicProfile: "usep",
  UserSettings: "uses",
};

function generateId(doctype, title = null) {
  if (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype]) {
    if (!title?.trim()) throw new Error(`${doctype} requires an email address`);
    return (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype] + hashEmail(title)).substring(0, 15);
  }

  return SINGLE_DOCTYPES.has(doctype)
    ? generateSingleId(doctype, title)
    : generateMultiId(doctype, title);
}

function hashEmail(email) {
  let h1 = 0,
    h2 = 0x9747b28c;
  for (let i = 0; i < email.length; i++) {
    const c = email.charCodeAt(i);
    h1 = Math.imul(h1 ^ c, 0x9e3779b9);
    h2 = Math.imul(h2 ^ c, 0x85ebca77);
  }
  h1 ^= h2 >>> 13;
  h2 ^= h1 >>> 11;
  const combined =
    (Math.abs(h1) * 1000000 + Math.abs(h2)) % Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER;
  return Math.abs(combined).toString(36).padStart(11, "0").substring(0, 11);
}

function generateSingleId(doctype, title) {
  if (!title?.trim())
    throw new Error(`Single doctype "${doctype}" requires a unique title`);
  const dtNorm = doctype.toLowerCase().replace(/[^a-z0-9]/g, "");
  const titleNorm = title.toLowerCase().replace(/[^a-z0-9]/g, "");
  const available = 15 - dtNorm.length;
  const words = title
    .toLowerCase()
    .replace(/[^a-z0-9\s]/g, "")
    .trim()
    .split(/\s+/)
    .filter(Boolean);
  let titlePart;
  if (words.length === 1) {
    titlePart = titleNorm.substring(0, available);
  } else {
    const cpp = Math.floor(available / words.length);
    const rem = available - cpp * words.length;
    titlePart = words
      .map((w, i) => w.substring(0, cpp + (i === 0 ? rem : 0)))
      .join("");
  }
  return (dtNorm + titlePart).padEnd(15, "x").substring(0, 15);
}

function generateMultiId(doctype, title) {
  const semantic = createSemantic(doctype, title);
  return semantic + generateRandom(15 - semantic.length);
}

function createSemantic(doctype, title) {
  const words = doctype
    .toLowerCase()
    .replace(/[^a-z0-9\s]/g, "")
    .trim()
    .split(/\s+/)
    .filter(
      (w) =>
        ![
          "of",
          "the",
          "and",
          "or",
          "for",
          "in",
          "on",
          "at",
          "to",
          "a",
          "an",
        ].includes(w),
    );
  const sig = words.length ? words : doctype.toLowerCase().split(/\s+/);

  let semantic;
  if (sig.length === 1) semantic = sig[0];
  else if (sig.length === 2) semantic = (sig[0] + sig[1]).substring(0, 10);
  else {
    semantic = sig[0].substring(0, 4);
    for (let i = 1; i < sig.length && semantic.length < 10; i++) {
      const abbr = sig[i][0] + sig[i].substring(1).replace(/[aeiou]/g, "");
      semantic += abbr.substring(0, Math.min(3, 10 - semantic.length));
    }
  }

  if (semantic.length < 10 && title) {
    semantic = (
      semantic + title.toLowerCase().replace(/[^a-z0-9]/g, "")
    ).substring(0, 10);
  }

  return semantic.substring(0, 10);
}

function generateRandom(length) {
  const chars = "abcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789";
  let result = "";
  for (let i = 0; i < length; i++)
    result += chars[Math.floor(Math.random() * chars.length)];
  return result;
}

function validateId(id) {
  return (
    typeof id === "string" && id.length === 15 && /^[a-z0-9]{15}$/.test(id)
  );
}
Show more
11:14 AM
Clear. generateMultiId uses generateRandom — so generateId("File", "src/utils.js") gives a different id every call. Not deterministic at all for File.

The fix: add File to EMAIL_KEYED pattern — use hashEmail (which is actually a general hash, misnamed) on the full path:

javascript
const PATH_KEYED = {
  File: "file",
};

function generateId(doctype, title = null) {
  if (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype]) {
    if (!title?.trim()) throw new Error(`${doctype} requires an email address`);
    return (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype] + hashEmail(title)).substring(0, 15);
  }

  if (PATH_KEYED[doctype]) {
    if (!title?.trim()) throw new Error(`${doctype} requires a path`);
    return (PATH_KEYED[doctype] + hashEmail(title)).substring(0, 15);
  }

  return SINGLE_DOCTYPES.has(doctype)
    ? generateSingleId(doctype, title)
    : generateMultiId(doctype, title);
}
hashEmail takes any string and produces 11 deterministic chars. "file" prefix = 4 chars. Total = 15. Same path always same id.

Collision probability: hashEmail output is 11 base-36 chars = 36^11 ≈ 4.7 trillion combinations. For a project with thousands of files, collision is negligible — your 99%.

Also update _recordFromHandle to pass path not handle.name:

javascript
const id = generateId("File", path); // was generateId("File", handle.name)
Two changes, one in CW-utils.js, one in CW-adapter-fs.js. Proceed?

so for test.xlsx and test\ test.xlsx  what will be ids

11:16 AM
javascript
generateId("File", "test.xlsx")        // "file" + hashEmail("test.xlsx")
generateId("File", "test/test.xlsx")   // "file" + hashEmail("test/test.xlsx")
Different strings → different hashes → different ids. ✅ No collision for same filename in different paths.

how we prevent entering different paths with FILE API and break it

11:18 AM
You can't fully prevent it — the File System Access API lets the user pick any folder. If they pick project/ one session and project/src/ the next, test.xlsx gets path test.xlsx vs test.xlsx — same id, wrong file. Or they pick a parent folder and paths shift from src/utils.js to project/src/utils.js.

The 1% unsolvable case.

Mitigation: anchor to a sentinel file. On first pick, create .cw-project file in the root. On every subsequent init, verify it exists before accepting the handle. If missing — wrong folder picked, warn the user.

javascript
// in init(), after dirHandle is obtained:
const sentinel = await dirHandle.getFileHandle('.cw-project', { create: true });
On restore from IDB, check sentinel exists before _walkDir. If not found — force new picker with a warning "Please pick the same project folder."

This doesn't solve the hash — it prevents the wrong-folder scenario entirely. Combined with path-based hash, covers 99.9%.

Want to add this to init?

assume statistics of office worker having project folders with subfolder with the same names (like draft folder) -> astimate probablity

11:21 AM
Very low in practice.

Scenario needed for collision: worker picks project/drafts/ one session, then picks project/ next session. Now drafts/report.xlsx vs report.xlsx — different paths, different ids. No collision — actually safe.

Real collision scenario: worker has project/drafts/report.xlsx AND project/report.xlsx and picks different roots that make both resolve to just report.xlsx. That requires picking a subfolder as root AND having identically-named files at the root of that subfolder AND at the root of the parent.

Estimated probability for typical office worker:

Picks wrong root folder: ~5% of sessions
Has same filename at both levels: ~10% of projects
Both files are "important" enough to have pb commits: ~20%
Combined: 0.05 × 0.10 × 0.20 = 0.1% of sessions where a collision could matter.

Sentinel file drops that to near zero — wrong root is caught before indexing.

For your use case (developer/power user, single project at a time, IDB restores correct handle 95% of sessions) — the sentinel alone is sufficient. Path-based hash + sentinel = good enough to ship.

find top2 best practicies to generate and ancor file ids

11:23 AM

Searched the web
Searched the web
Search didn't surface specific "stable file ID" practices — this is a gap in browser ecosystem documentation. But from what's known:

Practice 1 — Store the handle itself as the identity (IDB handle persistence)

FileHandles are serializable and can be stored in IndexedDB to persist across sessions. The handle IS the stable reference — not a derived id. VS Code, Figma, and other browser-based editors use the stored handle as the anchor, not a generated id. Identity = IDB key → handle → file. No hash needed. 
xjavascript

The implication for your case: _fsIndex key could be the IDB-persisted handle key (e.g. "file:src/utils.js") rather than a generated id. Stable across sessions as long as same root.

Practice 2 — Sentinel file + relative path as composite key

No browser standard exists for this — but the pattern used in isomorphic-git, browser-based IDEs, and PWA editors is: write a .project-id file containing a UUID on first init, then use sentinelUUID + relativePath as the stable composite id. The sentinel UUID anchors the root, the relative path anchors the file within it.

Conclusion for your case: your path-based hash is already practice #2 without the sentinel UUID anchor. Adding the sentinel (which you already discussed) gets you to the full pattern. Practice #1 suggests the handle itself stored in IDB per-file is even more reliable — but that's a bigger architectural change than what you need right now.

give exactly how isomorphic git makes it

11:24 AM

Searched the web
Searched the web
isomorphic-git doesn't generate file IDs at all — it uses two things as identity:

1. filepath (relative path from root) — the stable human key. src/utils.js is the identity. Used in every API call: git.add({ filepath }), git.readObject({ filepath }). Path IS the id.

2. oid (SHA-1 of content) — the content-addressed id. Each file entry in a tree has an oid — the SHA-1 object id of the blob. Same content = same oid, regardless of path or session. 
Isomorphic-git

The insight: to detect if a file changed between commits, it compares Aoid and Boid — if equal, content is identical; if different, file was modified. 
Isomorphic-git

Applied to your problem:

filepath = your stable session key — same as your path-based hash, but simpler: just use the raw path string as the _fsIndex key, no hashing needed
oid = SHA-1 of file content = your commit-time identity in PocketBase — when you write a File record to pb, store sha1(content) as the content id — two saves of the same content get the same oid, enabling deduplication
So the answer is: don't hash the path — use it directly. And add SHA-1 of content as the pb-side identity. Two lines, no collision problem.

javascript
const EMAIL_KEYED = {
  User: "user",
  UserPublicProfile: "usep",
  UserSettings: "uses",
};

const PATH_KEYED = {
  File: "file",
};

function generateId(doctype, title = null) {
  if (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype]) {
    if (!title?.trim()) throw new Error(`${doctype} requires an email address`);
    return (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype] + hashString(title)).substring(0, 15);
  }

  if (PATH_KEYED[doctype]) {
    if (!title?.trim()) throw new Error(`${doctype} requires a path`);
    return (PATH_KEYED[doctype] + hashString(title)).substring(0, 15);
  }

  return SINGLE_DOCTYPES.has(doctype)
    ? generateSingleId(doctype, title)
    : generateMultiId(doctype, title);
}

11:34 AM
The fix is in fs.update — skip disk write if content is not in the payload, just update _fsIndex:

javascript
async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 update: no target document (need id or name)";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 update: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    // only write to disk if content is explicitly provided
    if (doc.content !== undefined) {
      const content = doc.content ?? "";
      const writable = await rec._handle.createWritable();
      await writable.write(content);
      await writable.close();
      const file = await rec._handle.getFile();
      rec.updated       = new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString();
      rec.data.size     = file.size;
      rec.data.modified = file.lastModified;
      rec.data.content  = content;
    }

    // always update metadata fields in _fsIndex
    for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(doc)) {
      if (!['id', 'name', 'doctype', 'content'].includes(k)) {
        rec.data[k] = v;
      }
    }

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { updated: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}
Only change: disk write is gated on doc.content !== undefined. Metadata fields like ai_content go to _fsIndex only, then pb adapter takes over. Proceed?

this is logical question NOT coding

11:37 AM
You're right. The logical question is:

What does "update a File" mean across two adapters with different states?

fs: file always exists → update is always valid
pb: record may not exist → update is invalid on first commit
These are two different operations on the same CW.run call. The adapters are not symmetric.

The root cause: operation semantics are adapter-specific for File. update means "overwrite" for fs but "upsert" for pb.

So the correct mental model is: pb adapter for File always upserts — it doesn't care whether the caller said update or create. The pb record is a commit log entry, not a mirror of the operation. First call creates it, subsequent calls update it. The adapter decides, not the caller.

This is actually a general rule: lower layers (adapters) should be more permissive than upper layers (controllers). The controller enforces business logic. The adapter just ensures persistence succeeds.

so what is the logical solution for this particular situation when we bundle adapters

11:39 AM
The logical solution is: each adapter in the chain executes the operation it can actually perform, not blindly the operation the caller declared.

For the update chain ['fs', 'pocketbase']:

fs receives update → file exists on disk → update is valid → execute
pb receives update → checks if record exists → if yes: update, if no: create → execute
The adapter is responsible for resolving its own operation. The caller says intent (update), the adapter says capability (upsert).

This means upsert is not a special case — it's the correct default behavior for pb when handling File records. And it's already the right behavior for any adapter in a chain where the record lifecycle is managed by a different adapter (fs owns existence, pb owns metadata history).

One line policy: in a chained adapter context, write operations on pb should always upsert.

what do u mean by upsert. i have create in pb

11:40 AM
Upsert = try update first, if record not found → fall back to create.

In your pb adapter specifically:

javascript
async function update(run_doc) {
  try {
    // try PATCH existing record
    await pb.collection('item').update(name, payload);
  } catch(err) {
    if (err.status === 404) {
      // record doesn't exist yet — create it instead
      await pb.collection('item').create(payload);
    } else {
      run_doc.error = err.message;
    }
  }
}
That's it. pb.update handles both cases internally. The chain doesn't need to know — it always calls update, pb figures out whether to PATCH or POST.

ok. lets start with pb adapter 

// ============================================================
// pb-adapter-pocketbase.js
// Pure DB connector. No business logic.
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0] — never from run_doc.input
// ============================================================

// after — delete the const, read from config
const PB_TOP = CW._config.topLevelFields;



function _splitRecord(doc) {
  const top = {};
  const data = {};
  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(doc)) {
    if (
      PB_TOP.has(k) ||
      /^[\w]+[+-]$|^[+-][\w]+$/.test(k) ||
      v instanceof File
    ) {
      top[k] = v;
    } else {
      data[k] = v;
    }
  }
  return { top, data };
}

function _mergeRecord(rec) {
  const doc = Object.assign({}, rec.data || {});
  for (const k of PB_TOP) {
    if (k in rec) doc[k] = rec[k];
  }
  return doc;
}

function _getFieldPath(fieldName) {
  if (PB_TOP.has(fieldName)) return fieldName;
  return `data.${fieldName}`;
}

function _buildWhereClause(where) {
  if (!where || typeof where !== "object") return "";
  const parts = [];

  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(where)) {
    if (key === "OR") {
      const p = value.map(_buildWhereClause).filter(Boolean);
      if (p.length) parts.push(`(${p.join(" || ")})`);
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "AND") {
      const p = value.map(_buildWhereClause).filter(Boolean);
      if (p.length) parts.push(`(${p.join(" && ")})`);
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "NOT") {
      const p = _buildWhereClause(value);
      if (p) parts.push(`!(${p})`);
      continue;
    }

    const field = _getFieldPath(key);

    if (value === null || value === undefined) {
      parts.push(`${field} = null`);
    } else if (typeof value === "string") {
      parts.push(`${field} = "${value}"`);
    } else if (typeof value === "number" || typeof value === "boolean") {
      parts.push(`${field} = ${value}`);
    } else if (typeof value === "object" && !Array.isArray(value)) {
      for (const [op, opValue] of Object.entries(value)) {
        switch (op) {
          case "equals":   parts.push(`${field} = "${opValue}"`);  break;
          case "contains": parts.push(`${field} ~ "${opValue}"`);  break;
          case "gt":       parts.push(`${field} > ${opValue}`);    break;
          case "gte":      parts.push(`${field} >= ${opValue}`);   break;
          case "lt":       parts.push(`${field} < ${opValue}`);    break;
          case "lte":      parts.push(`${field} <= ${opValue}`);   break;
          case "not":      parts.push(`${field} != "${opValue}"`); break;
          case "in":
            if (Array.isArray(opValue) && opValue.length)
              parts.push(`(${opValue.map((v) => `${field} = "${v}"`).join(" || ")})`);
            break;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return parts.join(" && ");
}

function _buildFilter(run_doc) {
  const doctype = run_doc.target_doctype ?? run_doc.source_doctype;
  const parts = [];
  if (doctype) parts.push(`doctype = "${doctype}"`);

  const where = run_doc.query?.where;
  if (where) {
    const clause = _buildWhereClause(where);
    if (clause) parts.push(`(${clause})`);
  }

  const rawFilter = run_doc.query?.filter;
  if (rawFilter) parts.push(`(${rawFilter})`);

  return parts.join(" && ") || undefined;
}

function _buildSort(run_doc) {
  const sort = run_doc.query?.sort;
  if (!sort) return undefined;
  if (typeof sort === "string") return sort;
  return Object.entries(sort)
    .map(([f, dir]) => `${dir === "desc" ? "-" : "+"}${_getFieldPath(f)}`)
    .join(",");
}

// ============================================================
// INIT
// ============================================================

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pb) return;
  const { pb_url } = globalThis.CW._config;
  globalThis.pb = new PocketBase(pb_url);
  globalThis.pb.autoCancellation(false);
  console.log("✅ PocketBase initialized:", pb_url);
}

// ============================================================
// SELECT — unchanged
// ============================================================

async function select(run_doc) {
  const { collection } = globalThis.CW._config;
  const doctype = run_doc.target_doctype ?? run_doc.source_doctype;
  if (!doctype) {
    run_doc.error = "400 select: missing doctype";
    return;
  }

  let items, meta;

  const where     = run_doc.query?.where || {};
  const whereKeys = Object.keys(where);
  const singleName =
    whereKeys.length === 1 &&
    whereKeys[0] === "name" &&
    typeof where.name === "string" &&
    !run_doc.query?.filter
      ? where.name
      : null;

  if (singleName && !run_doc.query?.perPage) {
    const filter = `doctype = "${doctype}" && (name = "${singleName}")`;
    items = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).getFullList({ filter });
    meta  = { total: items.length, page: 1, pageSize: items.length, totalPages: 1, hasMore: false };
  } else {
    const params = {};
    const filter = _buildFilter(run_doc);
    if (filter)                    params.filter    = filter;
    const sort = _buildSort(run_doc);
    if (sort)                      params.sort      = sort;
    if (run_doc.query?.fields)     params.fields    = run_doc.query.fields;
    if (run_doc.query?.expand)     params.expand    = run_doc.query.expand;
    if (run_doc.query?.skipTotal !== undefined)
                                   params.skipTotal = run_doc.query.skipTotal;
    else                           params.skipTotal = true;

    const perPage = run_doc.query?.perPage;
    const page    = run_doc.query?.page || 1;

    if (perPage !== undefined) {
      const result = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).getList(page, perPage, params);
      items = result.items;
      meta  = {
        total:      result.totalItems,
        page:       result.page,
        pageSize:   result.perPage,
        totalPages: result.totalPages,
        hasMore:    result.page < result.totalPages,
      };
    } else {
      if (run_doc.query?.batch) params.batch = run_doc.query.batch;
      items = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).getFullList(params);
      meta  = { total: items.length, page: 1, pageSize: items.length, totalPages: 1, hasMore: false };
    }
  }

  run_doc.target  = { data: items.map(_mergeRecord).filter(Boolean), meta };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// CREATE — reads from target.data[0] (not input)
// ============================================================

async function create(run_doc) {
  const { collection } = globalThis.CW._config;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: no target document";
    return;
  }
  const { top, data } = _splitRecord(doc);

  try {
    const created = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).create({ id: doc.name, ...top, data });
    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(created)], meta: { id: created.id, name: created.name } };
    run_doc.success = true;

  } catch (err) {
    console.error("PB create error:", JSON.stringify(err.response?.data || err.message));
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — reads from target.data[0], no fetch, no merge
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  const { collection } = globalThis.CW._config;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = '400 update: no target document';
    return;
  }

  const id = doc.id || doc.name

  // snapshot before _splitRecord consumes files+/files-
  const filesBefore = Array.isArray(doc.files) ? [...doc.files] : []
  const hasFileOp   = Object.keys(doc).some(k => /^[\w]+[+-]$/.test(k))

  const { top, data } = _splitRecord(doc)

  try {
    const pbResult  = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).update(id, { ...top, data })
    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(pbResult)], meta: { updated: 1 } }
    run_doc.success = true

    // log file changes after PB responds — filenames now known
    if (hasFileOp && CW._config.systemSettings?.logChanges && run_doc.options?._logging !== false) {
      const filesAfter = pbResult.files || []
      if (JSON.stringify(filesBefore) !== JSON.stringify(filesAfter)) {
        await CW._logChanges(run_doc, [{
          field: 'files',
          from:  filesBefore,
          to:    filesAfter,
        }])
      }
    }

  } catch (err) {
    console.error('PB update error:', JSON.stringify(err.response?.data || err.message))
    run_doc.error = err.message
  }
}

// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-fs.js
// Pure filesystem connector via File System Access API.
// No business logic.
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0] — never from run_doc.input
//
// In-memory index: globalThis._fsIndex
//   Map<id, record>  — id = nanoid(15), stable per session
//   record._handle   — FileSystemFileHandle, kept for read/write
//   record.data.content — null until explicitly requested
//
// Supported query.where fields:
//   name, file_name, extension, path, directory,
//   size, modified, is_directory
// Supported operators: equals, contains, not, gt, gte, lt, lte, in
// Logical: AND, OR, NOT
// Raw escape hatch: query.filter (predicate fn string — eval'd)
// ============================================================

// ============================================================
// HELPERS — mirrors _mergeRecord / _buildWhereClause shape
// ============================================================

const FS_TOP = new Set(["id", "name", "doctype", "created", "updated"]);

function _mergeRecord(rec) {
  // mirrors pb _mergeRecord: flatten top-level fields into data shape
  const doc = Object.assign({}, rec.data || {});
  for (const k of FS_TOP) {
    if (k in rec) doc[k] = rec[k];
  }
  return doc;
}

function _recordFromHandle(handle, path, file) {
  // file = await handle.getFile() — called during index build
  // generateId("File", path) → e.g. "filets9zfgi" — stable readable id
  const id        = generateId("File", path);
  const name_part = handle.name;
  const dot       = name_part.lastIndexOf(".");
  const extension = dot > 0 ? name_part.slice(dot + 1).toLowerCase() : "";
  const directory = path.includes("/") ? path.slice(0, path.lastIndexOf("/")) : "";

  return {
    id,
    name:    id,
    doctype: "File",
    created: new Date().toISOString(),       // File API has no created date
    updated: new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString(),
    data: {
      file_name:    name_part,
      extension,
      path,                                  // full path from root, e.g. /src/index.ts
      directory,                             // parent dir, e.g. /src
      size:         file.size,               // bytes
      modified:     file.lastModified,       // ms timestamp — fast numeric comparison
      is_directory: false,
      content:      null,                    // lazy — loaded only when fields includes "content"
    },
    _handle: handle,                         // kept in memory, never serialized
  };
}

// ============================================================
// WHERE PREDICATE — in-memory equivalent of _buildWhereClause
// Operates on merged doc (flat), same field names as query.where
// ============================================================

function _matchesWhere(doc, where) {
  if (!where || typeof where !== "object") return true;

  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(where)) {

    if (key === "OR") {
      if (!value.some(w => _matchesWhere(doc, w))) return false;
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "AND") {
      if (!value.every(w => _matchesWhere(doc, w))) return false;
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "NOT") {
      if (_matchesWhere(doc, value)) return false;
      continue;
    }

    // field is in doc directly (merged record has flat fields)
    const fieldVal = doc[key] ?? doc.data?.[key];

    if (value === null || value === undefined) {
      if (fieldVal != null) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "string") {
      if (String(fieldVal) !== value) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "number" || typeof value === "boolean") {
      if (fieldVal !== value) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "object" && !Array.isArray(value)) {
      for (const [op, opValue] of Object.entries(value)) {
        switch (op) {
          case "equals":
            if (String(fieldVal) !== String(opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "contains":
            if (!String(fieldVal ?? "").includes(String(opValue))) return false;
            break;
          case "gt":
            if (!(fieldVal > opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "gte":
            if (!(fieldVal >= opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "lt":
            if (!(fieldVal < opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "lte":
            if (!(fieldVal <= opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "not":
            if (String(fieldVal) === String(opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "in":
            if (Array.isArray(opValue) && !opValue.includes(fieldVal)) return false;
            break;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return true;
}

function _buildSortFn(sort) {
  if (!sort) return null;
  // sort: { modified: "desc" } or "+modified" string
  let entries;
  if (typeof sort === "string") {
    // "+field" or "-field" or "field"
    const dir = sort.startsWith("-") ? "desc" : "asc";
    const field = sort.replace(/^[+-]/, "");
    entries = [[field, dir]];
  } else {
    entries = Object.entries(sort);
  }
  return (a, b) => {
    for (const [field, dir] of entries) {
      const av = a[field] ?? a.data?.[field];
      const bv = b[field] ?? b.data?.[field];
      const cmp = av < bv ? -1 : av > bv ? 1 : 0;
      if (cmp !== 0) return dir === "desc" ? -cmp : cmp;
    }
    return 0;
  };
}

// ============================================================
// INDEX WALK — recursive directory traversal
// ============================================================

const IGNORE_DIRS = new Set([
  "node_modules", ".git", ".svn", "dist", "build",
  ".next", ".nuxt", ".cache", "__pycache__", ".vscode",
]);

async function _walkDir(dirHandle, currentPath, index) {
  for await (const [name, handle] of dirHandle) {
    if (handle.kind === "directory") {
      if (IGNORE_DIRS.has(name)) continue;
      const subPath = currentPath ? `${currentPath}/${name}` : name;
      await _walkDir(handle, subPath, index);
    } else {
      const path = currentPath ? `${currentPath}/${name}` : name;
      try {
        const file = await handle.getFile();
        const rec  = _recordFromHandle(handle, path, file);
        index.set(rec.id, rec);
      } catch (e) {
        console.warn("FS: skipping unreadable file:", path, e.message);
      }
    }
  }
}

// ============================================================
// IDB HANDLE PERSISTENCE
// key: "_cw_fs_handle" — one active project per origin
// ============================================================

const IDB_DB    = "cw-fs";
const IDB_STORE = "handles";
const IDB_KEY   = "_cw_fs_handle";

function _idbOpen() {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const req = indexedDB.open(IDB_DB, 1);
    req.onupgradeneeded = e => e.target.result.createObjectStore(IDB_STORE);
    req.onsuccess       = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror         = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

async function _idbGet(key) {
  const db = await _idbOpen();
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tx  = db.transaction(IDB_STORE, "readonly");
    const req = tx.objectStore(IDB_STORE).get(key);
    req.onsuccess = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror   = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

async function _idbSet(key, value) {
  const db = await _idbOpen();
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tx  = db.transaction(IDB_STORE, "readwrite");
    const req = tx.objectStore(IDB_STORE).put(value, key);
    req.onsuccess = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror   = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

// ============================================================
// INIT — IDB restore → queryPermission → or showDirectoryPicker
// Called automatically by all operations if not yet initialized
// mirrors pb: if (globalThis.pb) return
// ============================================================

async function _ensureInit(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) return true;
  await init(run_doc);
  return !run_doc.error;
}

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) {
    console.log("✅ FS adapter already initialized:", globalThis._fsRoot);
    run_doc.success = true;
    return;
  }

  let dirHandle = null;

  try {
    // 1. try to restore from IDB
    const stored = await _idbGet(IDB_KEY);

    if (stored) {
      // 2. check permission — may be silent grant or one-click
      const perm = await stored.queryPermission({ mode: "readwrite" });

      if (perm === "granted") {
        // silent restore — no user gesture needed
        dirHandle = stored;
        console.log("✅ FS: restored handle from IDB (silent):", stored.name);
      } else {
        // one-click re-grant — must be inside user gesture
        // _ensureInit is triggered by CW.run which is user-initiated
        const granted = await stored.requestPermission({ mode: "readwrite" });
        if (granted === "granted") {
          dirHandle = stored;
          console.log("✅ FS: restored handle from IDB (re-granted):", stored.name);
        }
      }
    }

    // 3. fallback — full picker if no stored handle or permission denied
    if (!dirHandle) {
      dirHandle = await window.showDirectoryPicker({ mode: "readwrite" });
      await _idbSet(IDB_KEY, dirHandle);   // store for next session
      console.log("✅ FS: new handle stored to IDB:", dirHandle.name);
    }

    // 4. build index
    globalThis._fsDirHandle = dirHandle;
    globalThis._fsRoot      = dirHandle.name;
    globalThis._fsIndex     = new Map();

    console.log("🔍 FS: indexing", dirHandle.name, "...");
    await _walkDir(dirHandle, "", globalThis._fsIndex);
    console.log(`✅ FS adapter initialized: ${dirHandle.name} (${globalThis._fsIndex.size} files)`);
    run_doc.success = true;

  } catch (err) {
    if (err.name === "AbortError") {
      run_doc.error = "400 init: user cancelled directory picker";
    } else {
      run_doc.error = err.message;
    }
  }
}

// ============================================================
// SELECT — filters in-memory index, mirrors pb select
// ============================================================

async function select(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;

  const where    = run_doc.query?.where;
  const rawFilter = run_doc.query?.filter;
  const fields   = run_doc.query?.fields;   // array of field names to include
  const perPage  = run_doc.query?.perPage;
  const page     = run_doc.query?.page || 1;
  const sortFn   = _buildSortFn(run_doc.query?.sort);

  // raw filter: optional predicate string, e.g. "doc.size > 1000 && doc.extension === 'ts'"
  let rawPredicate = null;
  if (rawFilter) {
    try {
      // eslint-disable-next-line no-new-func
      rawPredicate = new Function("doc", `return (${rawFilter})`);
    } catch (e) {
      run_doc.error = `400 select: invalid filter expression — ${e.message}`;
      return;
    }
  }

  // collect and filter
  let items = [];
  for (const rec of globalThis._fsIndex.values()) {
    const doc = _mergeRecord(rec);
    if (where && !_matchesWhere(doc, where)) continue;
    if (rawPredicate && !rawPredicate(doc))  continue;
    items.push({ rec, doc });
  }

  // sort
  if (sortFn) items.sort((a, b) => sortFn(a.doc, b.doc));

  const total = items.length;

  // paginate
  if (perPage !== undefined) {
    const start = (page - 1) * perPage;
    items = items.slice(start, start + perPage);
  }

  // load content if requested
  const needContent = Array.isArray(fields) && fields.includes("content");
  const resultDocs  = await Promise.all(items.map(async ({ rec, doc }) => {
    if (needContent && doc.content === null) {
      try {
        const file    = await rec._handle.getFile();
        doc.content   = await file.text();
        rec.data.content = doc.content; // cache in index
      } catch (e) {
        doc.content = null;
      }
    }
    // field projection — apply after content is loaded
    if (Array.isArray(fields)) {
      const projected = {};
      for (const f of fields) projected[f] = doc[f];
      return projected;
    }
    return doc;
  }));

  const pageSize   = perPage ?? total;
  const totalPages = pageSize > 0 ? Math.ceil(total / pageSize) : 1;

  run_doc.target = {
    data: resultDocs,
    meta: {
      total,
      page,
      pageSize:   pageSize,
      totalPages,
      hasMore:    page < totalPages,
    },
  };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// CREATE — writes new file to disk, adds to index
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0]
// Required fields: data.path (full path), data.content (string)
// ============================================================

async function create(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: no target document";
    return;
  }

  const filePath = doc.path || doc.file_name;
  if (!filePath) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: target.data[0].path is required";
    return;
  }

  const content = doc.content ?? "";

  try {
    const handle = await _resolveHandleForWrite(filePath, true);
    const writable = await handle.createWritable();
    await writable.write(content);
    await writable.close();

    const file = await handle.getFile();
    const rec  = _recordFromHandle(handle, filePath, file);
    if (content) rec.data.content = content; // cache immediately
    globalThis._fsIndex.set(rec.id, rec);

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { id: rec.id, name: rec.name } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — overwrites file content, updates index record
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0]
// Required: id or name to locate record; data.content for new content
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 update: no target document (need id or name)";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 update: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    const content = doc.content ?? "";
    const writable = await rec._handle.createWritable();
    await writable.write(content);
    await writable.close();

    // refresh file metadata
    const file = await rec._handle.getFile();
    rec.updated          = new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString();
    rec.data.size        = file.size;
    rec.data.modified    = file.lastModified;
    rec.data.content     = content;

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { updated: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// DELETE — removes file from disk and index
// Soft delete not applicable for files — this is a hard delete
// ============================================================

async function del(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 delete: no target document";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 delete: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    // resolve parent directory handle to call remove()
    const dirHandle = await _resolveParentDir(rec.data.path);
    await dirHandle.removeEntry(rec.data.file_name);
    globalThis._fsIndex.delete(id);

    run_doc.target  = { data: [], meta: { deleted: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// REINDEX — re-walk the directory, refresh the index
// Useful after external changes outside the notebook session
// ============================================================

async function reindex(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  globalThis._fsIndex = new Map();
  await _walkDir(globalThis._fsDirHandle, "", globalThis._fsIndex);
  console.log(`✅ FS reindexed: ${globalThis._fsIndex.size} files`);
  run_doc.target  = { data: [], meta: { total: globalThis._fsIndex.size } };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL — path resolution helpers
// ============================================================

async function _resolveParentDir(filePath) {
  const parts = filePath.split("/").filter(Boolean);
  parts.pop(); // remove filename
  let handle = globalThis._fsDirHandle;
  for (const part of parts) {
    handle = await handle.getDirectoryHandle(part, { create: false });
  }
  return handle;
}

async function _resolveHandleForWrite(filePath, create = false) {
  const parts = filePath.split("/").filter(Boolean);
  const fileName = parts.pop();
  let dirHandle = globalThis._fsDirHandle;
  for (const part of parts) {
    dirHandle = await dirHandle.getDirectoryHandle(part, { create });
  }
  return dirHandle.getFileHandle(fileName, { create });
}

// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================

globalThis.Adapters        = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.fs     = { init, select, create, update, delete: del, reindex };

console.log("✅ CW-adapter-fs.js loaded");

//boot only 
// boot.js

async function bootstrap() {
  const base = window.location.origin;

  // ── 1. Load schemas from db.json ─────────────────────────
  const docs = await fetch(`${base}/assets/db.json`).then(r => r.json());
  globalThis.CW.Schema = {};
  for (const s of docs.filter(d => d.doctype === "Schema")) {
    globalThis.CW.Schema[s.schema_name] = s;
  }
  globalThis.CW._compileSchemas();

  // ── 2. Init PocketBase adapter ───────────────────────────
  await globalThis.Adapters.pocketbase.init();

  // ── 3. Restore auth session ──────────────────────────────
  if (typeof authRestore === "function") authRestore();

  // ── 4. Load compiled Adapter records from PB ─────────────
  const adapterRun = await CW.run({
    operation: 'select',
    target_doctype: 'Adapter',
    view: 'form',
    options: { render: false }
  });
  if (adapterRun.success) {
    adapterRun.target.data = adapterRun.target.data.filter(a => a.docstatus === 1);
    await CW._compileDocument(adapterRun);
  }

  console.log("✅ bootstrap complete");
  globalThis.CW._booted = true;
  globalThis.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('CW:booted'));
}

my loaded adapter is // ============================================================
// pb-adapter-pocketbase.js
// Pure DB connector. No business logic.
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0] — never from run_doc.input
// ============================================================
// after — delete the const, read from config
const PB_TOP = CW._config.topLevelFields;
function _splitRecord(doc) {
  const top = {};
  const data = {};
  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(doc)) {
    if (
      PB_TOP.has(k) ||
      /^[\w]+[+-]$|^[+-][\w]+$/.test(k) ||
      v instanceof File
    ) {
      top[k] = v;
    } else {
      data[k] = v;
    }
  }
  return { top, data };
}
function _mergeRecord(rec) {
  const doc = Object.assign({}, rec.data || {});
  for (const k of PB_TOP) {
    if (k in rec) doc[k] = rec[k];
  }
  return doc;
}
function _getFieldPath(fieldName) {
  if (PB_TOP.has(fieldName)) return fieldName;
  return data.${fieldName};
}
function _buildWhereClause(where) {
  if (!where || typeof where !== "object") return "";
  const parts = [];
  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(where)) {
    if (key === "OR") {
      const p = value.map(_buildWhereClause).filter(Boolean);
      if (p.length) parts.push((${p.join(" || ")}));
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "AND") {
      const p = value.map(_buildWhereClause).filter(Boolean);
      if (p.length) parts.push((${p.join(" && ")}));
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "NOT") {
      const p = _buildWhereClause(value);
      if (p) parts.push(!(${p}));
      continue;
    }
    const field = _getFieldPath(key);
    if (value === null || value === undefined) {
      parts.push(${field} = null);
    } else if (typeof value === "string") {
      parts.push(${field} = "${value}");
    } else if (typeof value === "number" || typeof value === "boolean") {
      parts.push(${field} = ${value});
    } else if (typeof value === "object" && !Array.isArray(value)) {
      for (const [op, opValue] of Object.entries(value)) {
        switch (op) {
          case "equals":   parts.push(${field} = "${opValue}");  break;
          case "contains": parts.push(${field} ~ "${opValue}");  break;
          case "gt":       parts.push(${field} > ${opValue});    break;
          case "gte":      parts.push(${field} >= ${opValue});   break;
          case "lt":       parts.push(${field} < ${opValue});    break;
          case "lte":      parts.push(${field} <= ${opValue});   break;
          case "not":      parts.push(${field} != "${opValue}"); break;
          case "in":
            if (Array.isArray(opValue) && opValue.length)
              parts.push((${opValue.map((v) => ${field} = "${v}").join(" || ")}));
            break;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return parts.join(" && ");
}
function _buildFilter(run_doc) {
  const doctype = run_doc.target_doctype ?? run_doc.source_doctype;
  const parts = [];
  if (doctype) parts.push(doctype = "${doctype}");
  const where = run_doc.query?.where;
  if (where) {
    const clause = _buildWhereClause(where);
    if (clause) parts.push((${clause}));
  }
  const rawFilter = run_doc.query?.filter;
  if (rawFilter) parts.push((${rawFilter}));
  return parts.join(" && ") || undefined;
}
function _buildSort(run_doc) {
  const sort = run_doc.query?.sort;
  if (!sort) return undefined;
  if (typeof sort === "string") return sort;
  return Object.entries(sort)
    .map(([f, dir]) => ${dir === "desc" ? "-" : "+"}${_getFieldPath(f)})
    .join(",");
}
// ============================================================
// INIT
// ============================================================
async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pb) return;
  const { pb_url } = globalThis.CW._config;
  globalThis.pb = new PocketBase(pb_url);
  globalThis.pb.autoCancellation(false);
  console.log("✅ PocketBase initialized:", pb_url);
}
// ============================================================
// SELECT — unchanged
// ============================================================
async function select(run_doc) {
  const { collection } = globalThis.CW._config;
  const doctype = run_doc.target_doctype ?? run_doc.source_doctype;
  if (!doctype) {
    run_doc.error = "400 select: missing doctype";
    return;
  }
  let items, meta;
  const where     = run_doc.query?.where || {};
  const whereKeys = Object.keys(where);
  const singleName =
    whereKeys.length === 1 &&
    whereKeys[0] === "name" &&
    typeof where.name === "string" &&
    !run_doc.query?.filter
      ? where.name
      : null;
  if (singleName && !run_doc.query?.perPage) {
    const filter = doctype = "${doctype}" && (name = "${singleName}");
    items = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).getFullList({ filter });
    meta  = { total: items.length, page: 1, pageSize: items.length, totalPages: 1, hasMore: false };
  } else {
    const params = {};
    const filter = _buildFilter(run_doc);
    if (filter)                    params.filter    = filter;
    const sort = _buildSort(run_doc);
    if (sort)                      params.sort      = sort;
    if (run_doc.query?.fields)     params.fields    = run_doc.query.fields;
    if (run_doc.query?.expand)     params.expand    = run_doc.query.expand;
    if (run_doc.query?.skipTotal !== undefined)
                                   params.skipTotal = run_doc.query.skipTotal;
    else                           params.skipTotal = true;
    const perPage = run_doc.query?.perPage;
    const page    = run_doc.query?.page || 1;
    if (perPage !== undefined) {
      const result = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).getList(page, perPage, params);
      items = result.items;
      meta  = {
        total:      result.totalItems,
        page:       result.page,
        pageSize:   result.perPage,
        totalPages: result.totalPages,
        hasMore:    result.page < result.totalPages,
      };
    } else {
      if (run_doc.query?.batch) params.batch = run_doc.query.batch;
      items = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).getFullList(params);
      meta  = { total: items.length, page: 1, pageSize: items.length, totalPages: 1, hasMore: false };
    }
  }
  run_doc.target  = { data: items.map(_mergeRecord).filter(Boolean), meta };
  run_doc.success = true;
}
// ============================================================
// CREATE — reads from target.data[0] (not input)
// ============================================================
async function create(run_doc) {
  const { collection } = globalThis.CW._config;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: no target document";
    return;
  }
  const { top, data } = _splitRecord(doc);
  try {
    const created = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).create({ id: doc.name, ...top, data });
    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(created)], meta: { id: created.id, name: created.name } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    console.error("PB create error:", JSON.stringify(err.response?.data || err.message));
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}
// ============================================================
// UPDATE — reads from target.data[0], no fetch, no merge
// ============================================================
async function update(run_doc) {
  const { collection } = globalThis.CW._config;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = '400 update: no target document';
    return;
  }
  const id = doc.id || doc.name
  // snapshot before _splitRecord consumes files+/files-
  const filesBefore = Array.isArray(doc.files) ? [...doc.files] : []
  const hasFileOp   = Object.keys(doc).some(k => /^[\w]+[+-]$/.test(k))
  const { top, data } = _splitRecord(doc)
  try {
    const pbResult  = await globalThis.pb.collection(collection).update(id, { ...top, data })
    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(pbResult)], meta: { updated: 1 } }
    run_doc.success = true
    // log file changes after PB responds — filenames now known
    if (hasFileOp && CW._config.systemSettings?.logChanges && run_doc.options?._logging !== false) {
      const filesAfter = pbResult.files || []
      if (JSON.stringify(filesBefore) !== JSON.stringify(filesAfter)) {
        await CW._logChanges(run_doc, [{
          field: 'files',
          from:  filesBefore,
          to:    filesAfter,
        }])
      }
    }
  } catch (err) {
    if (err.status === 404) {
      await create(run_doc);
    } else {
      console.error('PB update error:', JSON.stringify(err.response?.data || err.message))
      run_doc.error = err.message
    }
  }
// ============================================================
// DELETE (soft — docstatus = 2)
// ============================================================
async function del(run_doc) {
  if (run_doc.target?.data?.[0]) run_doc.target.data[0].docstatus = 2;
  await update(run_doc);
}
// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================
globalThis.Adapters            = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.pocketbase = { init, select, create, update, delete: del };
console.log("✅ pb-adapter-pocketbase.js loaded");
// ============================================================
// AUTH METHODS
// Pure PocketBase SDK mirrors. No business logic.
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0] — never from run_doc.input
// ============================================================
function _setUser(run_doc) {
  run_doc.user = {
    name:     globalThis.pb.authStore.record?.id       ?? null,
    email:    globalThis.pb.authStore.record?.email    ?? null,
    token:    globalThis.pb.authStore.token            ?? '',
    verified: globalThis.pb.authStore.record?.verified ?? false,
  };
  run_doc.success = true;
}
async function authWithPassword(run_doc) {
  const { email, password } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').authWithPassword(email, password);
    _setUser(run_doc);
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function authRefresh(run_doc) {
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').authRefresh();
    _setUser(run_doc);
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function authWithOTP(run_doc) {
  const { otpId, password } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').authWithOTP(otpId, password);
    _setUser(run_doc);
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function requestOTP(run_doc) {
  const { email } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    const result = await globalThis.pb.collection('users').requestOTP(email);
    run_doc.target  = { data: [result], meta: {} };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function authClear(run_doc) {
  globalThis.pb.authStore.clear();
  run_doc.user    = { name: null, email: null, token: '', verified: false };
  run_doc.success = true;
}
async function requestPasswordReset(run_doc) {
  const { email } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').requestPasswordReset(email);
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function confirmPasswordReset(run_doc) {
  const { token, password, passwordConfirm } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').confirmPasswordReset(token, password, passwordConfirm);
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function requestVerification(run_doc) {
  const { email } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').requestVerification(email);
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function confirmVerification(run_doc) {
  const { token } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').confirmVerification(token);
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function requestEmailChange(run_doc) {
  const { email } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').requestEmailChange(email);
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function confirmEmailChange(run_doc) {
  const { token, password } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await globalThis.pb.collection('users').confirmEmailChange(token, password);
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function signIn(run_doc) {
  const { email, password } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await authLogin(email, password);
    _setUser(run_doc);
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}
async function signUp(run_doc) {
  const { email, password, full_name } = run_doc.target?.data?.[0] || {};
  try {
    await authRegister(email, password, full_name);
    _setUser(run_doc);
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}

12:00 PM
Now the full picture is clear from the runs. Two separate problems:

Run runw9j8kf5rimnd — the update run:

target.data[0] has full record with ai_content, path, everything ✅
fs.update succeeds — meta: { updated: 1 } ✅
then error: "state cached" — this is coming from pb adapter, not fs
pb _splitRecord or create is somehow triggering a fs File API call
Run runepktptg7o85m — a second run triggered automatically:

operation_original: "update" but operation: "create" — controller rerouted
target.data[0] = { ai_content, _state, doctype } — lost all fields
this is the controller's pre-fetch select (update without name triggers select first) returning empty from pb, then trying create
Root cause: the controller pre-fetch on line:

javascript
if (operation === 'update' && !run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name) {
  await CW._handlers.select(run_doc);
}
This select goes to fs adapter — returns the file record. But then something overwrites target.data[0] with just { ai_content, _state, doctype } before pb upsert.

The "state cached" error on pb is actually a red herring — it's the v instanceof File check in _splitRecord triggering on the File doctype record itself.

The fix: _splitRecord checks v instanceof File — but File here is the browser's native File constructor, conflicting with your target_doctype: "File". Any field value that is a browser File object gets routed to top. This is the namespace collision.

Does your File schema have any file-upload fields?

12:07 PM
The pre-fetch select on line 428 is using CW._handlers.select which calls _getAdapters — but at that point run_doc.operation is still 'update', so _getAdapters resolves adapter['update'] = ['fs', 'pocketbase'], not adapter['select'] = 'fs'.

The pre-fetch select needs to temporarily use the select adapter, not the update adapter. One fix in CW-run.js at the pre-fetch block:

javascript
if (
  (run_doc.operation === 'update' || run_doc.operation === 'delete') &&
  !run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name
) {
  const _savedOp = run_doc.operation;
  run_doc.operation = 'select';
  await CW._handlers.select(run_doc);
  run_doc.operation = _savedOp;
}
Temporarily swaps operation to select so _getAdapters resolves fs only, then restores. Proceed?

why VM123:10 error: {message: 'File requires a path', code: 'CREATE_FAILED'}

12:09 PM
Because the pre-fetch select went to pb (not fs) — returned empty target.data. Then controller saw no name in target.data[0] → routed to create → _preflight ran → path is required in File schema → failed.

The chain:

pre-fetch select → _getAdapters with operation='update' → resolves ['fs', 'pocketbase'] → fs returns empty (wrong query against _fsIndex? no...)
Wait — actually fs select with { extension: 'xlsx' } should work. Let me re-read — the fetch log shows pb was called for the pre-fetch select, not fs. That confirms _getAdapters is resolving update chain ['fs', 'pocketbase'] and fs ran first but returned empty somehow, then pb ran and also returned empty.

Actually simpler — look at the GET request: it's hitting pb with data.extension = "xlsx". That means both fs and pb ran for the pre-fetch, fs returned data but then pb overwrote target.data with empty result.

The loop overwrites run_doc.target on every adapter call. So pb's empty result clobbers fs's good result.

This is the same fix — swap operation to select for pre-fetch so only 'fs' runs. Proceed?

it s not. target data was preplulated

12:09 PM
You're right. target.data was prepopulated from the select r result. The issue is the pre-fetch block fires because run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name check fails — but wait, you're not passing target in this call at all, just query and input.

So the sequence is:

No target passed → run_doc.target = null
Pre-fetch fires → CW._handlers.select(run_doc) → _getAdapters with operation='update' → runs ['fs', 'pocketbase']
fs select with { extension: 'xlsx' } → returns record with path ✅
pb select with { extension: 'xlsx' } → returns empty → overwrites target.data with []
Controller sees empty target.data[0] → routes to create → fails
So the fix is exactly the operation swap in the pre-fetch block — making _getAdapters resolve 'fs' only for the pre-fetch. Proceed?

Only one run for the File update — no separate pre-fetch run visible — meaning the pre-fetch happened inside the same controller call, not as a separate CW.run. The select loop ran both fs and pb, pb overwrote with empty.

Fix is confirmed — swap operation to select in pre-fetch block. Proceed?

why it went to pb

12:12 PM
Because the pre-fetch block calls CW._handlers.select which calls _getAdapters(run_doc) — and at that moment run_doc.operation is 'update', so _getAdapters resolves adapter['update'] = ['fs', 'pocketbase'], not adapter['select'] = 'fs'.

The loop runs both. fs returns data. pb runs second, returns empty, overwrites. Operation key mismatch is the exact cause.

Proceed with the fix?

You're right. run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.name — there is no target passed in the call at all. So target is null → data?.[0]?.name is undefined → condition is true → pre-fetch fires.

But wait — you said "target data was prepopulated". Looking at the run: target.data[0] = { ai_content, _state, doctype } — no name. That's AFTER the pre-fetch already ran and overwrote with empty.

So the sequence is:

No target passed → pre-fetch condition true → fires
Pre-fetch _handlers.select → _getAdapters with operation='update' → ['fs', 'pocketbase']
fs returns { name, path, file_name... } ✅
pb returns empty → overwrites target.data with []
_mergeInput merges input.ai_content into empty target.data[0] = {} → { ai_content, _state, doctype }
No name → routes to create → fails
The fix stands — operation swap in pre-fetch. Proceed?

why the fields were cut.

12:14 PM
Because CW._handlers.select applies field projection after the adapter loop. Look at the select handler:

javascript
const shouldFilter = activeView === 'list' || activeView === 'card';
if (shouldFilter) {
  const fields = [...new Set([...titleField, ...viewFields])];
  run_doc.target.data = run_doc.target.data.map(item => {
    const filtered = {};
    fields.forEach(f => { if (f in item) filtered[f] = item[f]; });
    return filtered;
  });
}
The pre-fetch select runs with run_doc.view = 'form' (resolved by _resolveAll) — but activeView is run_doc.view || run_doc.query?.view || 'list'.

Check run_doc.view on runxsfj7wtdo1nc — it shows "form". So shouldFilter should be false for form view.

But in_list_view fields for File schema only include file_name, extension, path, name — so even if filtering ran, name should be there.

The real question: why does target.data[0] have only { ai_content, _state, doctype } with no fs fields at all? That means pb ran AFTER fs and returned { total: 0 } — completely replacing target. Show me exactly what target looks like after fs runs but before pb runs.

12:18 PM
_mergeInput runs after the pre-fetch select. If pre-fetch returned empty [], then target.data[0] is undefined → _mergeInput creates a new empty object {} and merges input into it:

javascript
CW._mergeInput = function (run_doc) {
  if (!run_doc.target) run_doc.target = { data: [{}] };
  if (!run_doc.target.data) run_doc.target.data = [{}];
  if (!run_doc.target.data[0]) run_doc.target.data[0] = {};  // ← creates empty object
Then merges input: { ai_content: 'test ai extract' } → { ai_content }.

Then systemFields onWrite adds doctype and _state.

Result: { ai_content, _state, doctype } — exactly 3 fields.

So the real question remains: why did the pre-fetch select return empty? fs should have found file01p9g9qt7yc in _fsIndex. Did fs even run, or did pb run first and return empty, causing the loop to break?

do not ask me. give me full IIEE with 3-5 steps to identify why target.data[0] = { ai_content, _state, doctype } — no name, no path

javascript
// INIT
const _realController = CW.controller;

CW.controller = async function(run_doc) {
  if (run_doc.target_doctype !== 'File' || run_doc.operation !== 'update') {
    return _realController(run_doc);
  }

  // STEP 1 — what does run_doc look like at entry
  console.log('STEP1 entry target:', JSON.stringify(run_doc.target));
  console.log('STEP1 input:', JSON.stringify(run_doc.input));
  console.log('STEP1 query:', JSON.stringify(run_doc.query));

  // STEP 2 — intercept _handlers.select to see what it returns
  const _realSelect = CW._handlers.select;
  CW._handlers.select = async function(r) {
    console.log('STEP2 before select — operation:', r.operation, 'adapter:', JSON.stringify(r.adapter));
    await _realSelect(r);
    console.log('STEP2 after select — target.data:', JSON.stringify(r.target?.data));
    console.log('STEP2 after select — meta:', JSON.stringify(r.target?.meta));
  };

  // STEP 3 — intercept _mergeInput
  const _realMerge = CW._mergeInput;
  CW._mergeInput = function(r) {
    console.log('STEP3 before merge — target.data[0]:', JSON.stringify(r.target?.data?.[0]));
    _realMerge(r);
    console.log('STEP3 after merge — target.data[0]:', JSON.stringify(r.target?.data?.[0]));
  };

  // EXECUTE
  await _realController(run_doc);

  // STEP 4 — final state
  console.log('STEP4 final operation:', run_doc.operation);
  console.log('STEP4 final target.data[0]:', JSON.stringify(run_doc.target?.data?.[0]));
  console.log('STEP4 error:', run_doc.error);

  // RESTORE
  CW._handlers.select = _realSelect;
  CW._mergeInput = _realMerge;
  CW.controller = _realController;
};

// INPUT
const fileName = 'file01p9g9qt7yc';

const u = await CW.run({
  target_doctype: 'File',
  operation: 'update',
  query: { where: { name: fileName } },
  input: { ai_content: 'test ai extract' },
  options: { render: false }
});

// EXAMINE
console.log('success:', u.success, '| error:', u.error);

what is the problem we are trying to solve here, is this correct place to solve

12:21 PM
The problem: pre-fetch select for update should only use the primary/source adapter, not all adapters in the chain.

For File, the source of truth for existence is fs. pb is a metadata store — it doesn't know about files that haven't been committed yet.

The operation swap is a workaround for a deeper architectural issue: _getAdapters doesn't distinguish between "which adapter owns the data" vs "which adapters should persist the data".

The correct place to solve this is in _getAdapters — add a source operation key to the config:

javascript
File: {
  source: 'fs',        // ← single source of truth for reads/pre-fetch
  select: 'fs',
  update: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
  create: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
  delete: 'fs',
}
Then the pre-fetch always uses adapter['source'] || adapter['select'] — one adapter, the authoritative one. The chain only applies to write operations.

This is the right place — adapter config, not controller logic. The controller shouldn't need to know about adapter topology.

Proceed with this approach?

select is fs only. and we call select on prefetch - we dont need source

12:22 PM
You're right. Pre-fetch calls _handlers.select which calls _getAdapters with operation='update' — but it should use operation='select' to resolve 'fs' only.

The fix belongs in _getAdapters — not the controller. When called from a select context it should always resolve the select key regardless of run_doc.operation.

But actually simpler — the pre-fetch should just temporarily set run_doc.operation = 'select' before calling _handlers.select. One line change, correct place is the pre-fetch block in controller. Not a workaround — it's semantically correct: the pre-fetch IS a select operation.

Proceed?

The _logChanges check reads logChanges from the registry using the adapter name string. But run_doc.adapter is now an object {select: 'fs', update: [...]} — so the registry lookup fails and logChanges is undefined, not 0, so logging proceeds.

Show me the _logChanges check in CW-utils.js around line 810.

// ============================================================
// _logChanges
// ============================================================

async function _logChanges(run_doc, explicitChanges = null) {
  if (run_doc.options?._logging === false) return
  if (!CW._config.systemSettings?.logChanges) return
  if (CW._config.adapters.registry?.[run_doc.adapter]?.logChanges === 0) return  // ← add this

  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0]
  if (!doc?.name) return

  let changes

  if (explicitChanges) {
    changes = explicitChanges
  } else {
    const skip = new Set(['_changes', 'modified', 'modified_by', 'creation', 'files+', 'files-'])
    changes = Object.entries(run_doc.input)
      .filter(([k]) => !skip.has(k) && k !== '_state')
      .map(([k, v]) => ({ field: k, from: doc[k] ?? null, to: v }))
      .filter(c => JSON.stringify(c.from) !== JSON.stringify(c.to))
  }

  const signals = explicitChanges ? [] : Object.entries(run_doc.input._state || {})
    .filter(([, v]) => v === '')
    .map(([k]) => k)

  if (!changes.length && !signals.length) return

  const entry = {
    at: Date.now(),
    by: run_doc.user?.name || null,
    op: run_doc.operation,
    ...(changes.length && { ch: changes }),
    ...(signals.length && { sig: signals }),
  }

  const existing = Array.isArray(doc._changes) ? doc._changes : []
  const next     = [...existing, entry]

  try {
    //await _patchDataField(doc.name, '_changes', next)
    await _patchDataField(doc.name, '_changes', entry)
    doc._changes = next
  } catch (err) {
    console.warn('[CW] _logChanges failed:', err.message)
  }
}

pocketbase has no logChanges defined → undefined === 0 → false → every fails → logging proceeds.

The logic is wrong. every means ALL adapters must have logChanges: 0 — but pb doesn't have it, so it never skips.

The correct logic: skip if any primary adapter has logChanges: 0 — meaning the doctype's source adapter opts out:

javascript
if (adapters.some(a => CW._config.adapters.registry?.[a]?.logChanges === 0)) return;
