// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-fs.js
// Pure filesystem connector via File System Access API.
// No business logic.
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0] — never from run_doc.input
//
// In-memory index: globalThis._fsIndex
//   Map<id, record>  — id = nanoid(15), stable per session
//   record._handle   — FileSystemFileHandle, kept for read/write
//   record.data.content — null until explicitly requested
//
// Supported query.where fields:
//   name, file_name, extension, path, directory,
//   size, modified, is_directory
// Supported operators: equals, contains, not, gt, gte, lt, lte, in
// Logical: AND, OR, NOT
// Raw escape hatch: query.filter (predicate fn string — eval'd)
// ============================================================

// ============================================================
// HELPERS — mirrors _mergeRecord / _buildWhereClause shape
// ============================================================

const FS_TOP = new Set(["id", "name", "doctype", "created", "updated"]);

function _mergeRecord(rec) {
  // mirrors pb _mergeRecord: flatten top-level fields into data shape
  const doc = Object.assign({}, rec.data || {});
  for (const k of FS_TOP) {
    if (k in rec) doc[k] = rec[k];
  }
  return doc;
}

function _recordFromHandle(handle, path, file) {
  // file = await handle.getFile() — called during index build
  // generateId("File", path) → e.g. "filets9zfgi" — stable readable id
  const id        = generateId("File", path);
  const name_part = handle.name;
  const dot       = name_part.lastIndexOf(".");
  const extension = dot > 0 ? name_part.slice(dot + 1).toLowerCase() : "";
  const directory = path.includes("/") ? path.slice(0, path.lastIndexOf("/")) : "";

  return {
    id,
    name:    id,
    doctype: "File",
    created: new Date().toISOString(),       // File API has no created date
    updated: new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString(),
    data: {
      file_name:    name_part,
      extension,
      path,                                  // full path from root, e.g. /src/index.ts
      directory,                             // parent dir, e.g. /src
      size:         file.size,               // bytes
      modified:     file.lastModified,       // ms timestamp — fast numeric comparison
      is_directory: false,
      content:      null,                    // lazy — loaded only when fields includes "content"
    },
    _handle: handle,                         // kept in memory, never serialized
  };
}

// ============================================================
// WHERE PREDICATE — in-memory equivalent of _buildWhereClause
// Operates on merged doc (flat), same field names as query.where
// ============================================================

function _matchesWhere(doc, where) {
  if (!where || typeof where !== "object") return true;

  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(where)) {

    if (key === "OR") {
      if (!value.some(w => _matchesWhere(doc, w))) return false;
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "AND") {
      if (!value.every(w => _matchesWhere(doc, w))) return false;
      continue;
    }
    if (key === "NOT") {
      if (_matchesWhere(doc, value)) return false;
      continue;
    }

    // field is in doc directly (merged record has flat fields)
    const fieldVal = doc[key] ?? doc.data?.[key];

    if (value === null || value === undefined) {
      if (fieldVal != null) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "string") {
      if (String(fieldVal) !== value) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "number" || typeof value === "boolean") {
      if (fieldVal !== value) return false;
    } else if (typeof value === "object" && !Array.isArray(value)) {
      for (const [op, opValue] of Object.entries(value)) {
        switch (op) {
          case "equals":
            if (String(fieldVal) !== String(opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "contains":
            if (!String(fieldVal ?? "").includes(String(opValue))) return false;
            break;
          case "gt":
            if (!(fieldVal > opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "gte":
            if (!(fieldVal >= opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "lt":
            if (!(fieldVal < opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "lte":
            if (!(fieldVal <= opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "not":
            if (String(fieldVal) === String(opValue)) return false;
            break;
          case "in":
            if (Array.isArray(opValue) && !opValue.includes(fieldVal)) return false;
            break;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return true;
}

function _buildSortFn(sort) {
  if (!sort) return null;
  // sort: { modified: "desc" } or "+modified" string
  let entries;
  if (typeof sort === "string") {
    // "+field" or "-field" or "field"
    const dir = sort.startsWith("-") ? "desc" : "asc";
    const field = sort.replace(/^[+-]/, "");
    entries = [[field, dir]];
  } else {
    entries = Object.entries(sort);
  }
  return (a, b) => {
    for (const [field, dir] of entries) {
      const av = a[field] ?? a.data?.[field];
      const bv = b[field] ?? b.data?.[field];
      const cmp = av < bv ? -1 : av > bv ? 1 : 0;
      if (cmp !== 0) return dir === "desc" ? -cmp : cmp;
    }
    return 0;
  };
}

// ============================================================
// INDEX WALK — recursive directory traversal
// ============================================================

const IGNORE_DIRS = new Set([
  "node_modules", ".git", ".svn", "dist", "build",
  ".next", ".nuxt", ".cache", "__pycache__", ".vscode",
]);

async function _walkDir(dirHandle, currentPath, index) {
  for await (const [name, handle] of dirHandle) {
    if (handle.kind === "directory") {
      if (IGNORE_DIRS.has(name)) continue;
      const subPath = currentPath ? `${currentPath}/${name}` : name;
      await _walkDir(handle, subPath, index);
    } else {
      const path = currentPath ? `${currentPath}/${name}` : name;
      try {
        const file = await handle.getFile();
        const rec  = _recordFromHandle(handle, path, file);
        index.set(rec.id, rec);
      } catch (e) {
        console.warn("FS: skipping unreadable file:", path, e.message);
      }
    }
  }
}

// ============================================================
// IDB HANDLE PERSISTENCE
// key: "_cw_fs_handle" — one active project per origin
// ============================================================

const IDB_DB    = "cw-fs";
const IDB_STORE = "handles";
const IDB_KEY   = "_cw_fs_handle";

function _idbOpen() {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const req = indexedDB.open(IDB_DB, 1);
    req.onupgradeneeded = e => e.target.result.createObjectStore(IDB_STORE);
    req.onsuccess       = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror         = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

async function _idbGet(key) {
  const db = await _idbOpen();
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tx  = db.transaction(IDB_STORE, "readonly");
    const req = tx.objectStore(IDB_STORE).get(key);
    req.onsuccess = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror   = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

async function _idbSet(key, value) {
  const db = await _idbOpen();
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tx  = db.transaction(IDB_STORE, "readwrite");
    const req = tx.objectStore(IDB_STORE).put(value, key);
    req.onsuccess = e => resolve(e.target.result);
    req.onerror   = e => reject(e.target.error);
  });
}

// ============================================================
// INIT — IDB restore → queryPermission → or showDirectoryPicker
// Called automatically by all operations if not yet initialized
// mirrors pb: if (globalThis.pb) return
// ============================================================

async function _ensureInit(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) return true;
  await init(run_doc);
  return !run_doc.error;
}

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) {
    console.log("✅ FS adapter already initialized:", globalThis._fsRoot);
    run_doc.success = true;
    return;
  }

  let dirHandle = null;

  try {
    // 1. try to restore from IDB
    const stored = await _idbGet(IDB_KEY);

    if (stored) {
      // 2. check permission — may be silent grant or one-click
      const perm = await stored.queryPermission({ mode: "readwrite" });

      if (perm === "granted") {
        // silent restore — no user gesture needed
        dirHandle = stored;
        console.log("✅ FS: restored handle from IDB (silent):", stored.name);
      } else {
        // one-click re-grant — must be inside user gesture
        // _ensureInit is triggered by CW.run which is user-initiated
        const granted = await stored.requestPermission({ mode: "readwrite" });
        if (granted === "granted") {
          dirHandle = stored;
          console.log("✅ FS: restored handle from IDB (re-granted):", stored.name);
        }
      }
    }

    // 3. fallback — full picker if no stored handle or permission denied
    if (!dirHandle) {
      dirHandle = await window.showDirectoryPicker({ mode: "readwrite" });
      await _idbSet(IDB_KEY, dirHandle);   // store for next session
      console.log("✅ FS: new handle stored to IDB:", dirHandle.name);
    }

    // 4. build index
    globalThis._fsDirHandle = dirHandle;
    globalThis._fsRoot      = dirHandle.name;
    globalThis._fsIndex     = new Map();

    console.log("🔍 FS: indexing", dirHandle.name, "...");
    await _walkDir(dirHandle, "", globalThis._fsIndex);
    console.log(`✅ FS adapter initialized: ${dirHandle.name} (${globalThis._fsIndex.size} files)`);
    run_doc.success = true;

  } catch (err) {
    if (err.name === "AbortError") {
      run_doc.error = "400 init: user cancelled directory picker";
    } else {
      run_doc.error = err.message;
    }
  }
}

// ============================================================
// SELECT — filters in-memory index, mirrors pb select
// ============================================================

async function select(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;

  const where    = run_doc.query?.where;
  const rawFilter = run_doc.query?.filter;
  const fields   = run_doc.query?.fields;   // array of field names to include
  const perPage  = run_doc.query?.perPage;
  const page     = run_doc.query?.page || 1;
  const sortFn   = _buildSortFn(run_doc.query?.sort);

  // raw filter: optional predicate string, e.g. "doc.size > 1000 && doc.extension === 'ts'"
  let rawPredicate = null;
  if (rawFilter) {
    try {
      // eslint-disable-next-line no-new-func
      rawPredicate = new Function("doc", `return (${rawFilter})`);
    } catch (e) {
      run_doc.error = `400 select: invalid filter expression — ${e.message}`;
      return;
    }
  }

  // collect and filter
  let items = [];
  for (const rec of globalThis._fsIndex.values()) {
    const doc = _mergeRecord(rec);
    if (where && !_matchesWhere(doc, where)) continue;
    if (rawPredicate && !rawPredicate(doc))  continue;
    items.push({ rec, doc });
  }

  // sort
  if (sortFn) items.sort((a, b) => sortFn(a.doc, b.doc));

  const total = items.length;

  // paginate
  if (perPage !== undefined) {
    const start = (page - 1) * perPage;
    items = items.slice(start, start + perPage);
  }

  // load content if requested
  const needContent = Array.isArray(fields) && fields.includes("content");
  const resultDocs  = await Promise.all(items.map(async ({ rec, doc }) => {
    if (needContent && doc.content === null) {
      try {
        const file    = await rec._handle.getFile();
        doc.content   = await file.text();
        rec.data.content = doc.content; // cache in index
      } catch (e) {
        doc.content = null;
      }
    }
    // field projection — apply after content is loaded
    if (Array.isArray(fields)) {
      const projected = {};
      for (const f of fields) projected[f] = doc[f];
      return projected;
    }
    return doc;
  }));

  const pageSize   = perPage ?? total;
  const totalPages = pageSize > 0 ? Math.ceil(total / pageSize) : 1;

  run_doc.target = {
    data: resultDocs,
    meta: {
      total,
      page,
      pageSize:   pageSize,
      totalPages,
      hasMore:    page < totalPages,
    },
  };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// CREATE — writes new file to disk, adds to index
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0]
// Required fields: data.path (full path), data.content (string)
// ============================================================

async function create(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: no target document";
    return;
  }

  const filePath = doc.path || doc.file_name;
  if (!filePath) {
    run_doc.error = "400 create: target.data[0].path is required";
    return;
  }

  const content = doc.content ?? "";

  try {
    const handle = await _resolveHandleForWrite(filePath, true);
    const writable = await handle.createWritable();
    await writable.write(content);
    await writable.close();

    const file = await handle.getFile();
    const rec  = _recordFromHandle(handle, filePath, file);
    if (content) rec.data.content = content; // cache immediately
    globalThis._fsIndex.set(rec.id, rec);

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { id: rec.id, name: rec.name } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — overwrites file content, updates index record
// Reads from run_doc.target.data[0]
// Required: id or name to locate record; data.content for new content
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 update: no target document (need id or name)";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 update: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    // only write to disk if content explicitly provided
    if (doc.content !== undefined && doc.content !== null) {
      const content  = doc.content ?? "";
      const writable = await rec._handle.createWritable();
      await writable.write(content);
      await writable.close();
      const file        = await rec._handle.getFile();
      rec.updated       = new Date(file.lastModified).toISOString();
      rec.data.size     = file.size;
      rec.data.modified = file.lastModified;
      rec.data.content  = content;
    }

    // always update metadata fields in _fsIndex
    for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(doc)) {
      if (!['id', 'name', 'doctype', 'content'].includes(k)) {
        rec.data[k] = v;
      }
    }

    run_doc.target  = { data: [_mergeRecord(rec)], meta: { updated: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// DELETE — removes file from disk and index
// Soft delete not applicable for files — this is a hard delete
// ============================================================

async function del(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.id && !doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = "400 delete: no target document";
    return;
  }

  const id  = doc.id || doc.name;
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex.get(id);
  if (!rec) {
    run_doc.error = `404 delete: record not found — ${id}`;
    return;
  }

  try {
    // resolve parent directory handle to call remove()
    const dirHandle = await _resolveParentDir(rec.data.path);
    await dirHandle.removeEntry(rec.data.file_name);
    globalThis._fsIndex.delete(id);

    run_doc.target  = { data: [], meta: { deleted: 1 } };
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// REINDEX — re-walk the directory, refresh the index
// Useful after external changes outside the notebook session
// ============================================================

async function reindex(run_doc) {
  if (!await _ensureInit(run_doc)) return;
  globalThis._fsIndex = new Map();
  await _walkDir(globalThis._fsDirHandle, "", globalThis._fsIndex);
  console.log(`✅ FS reindexed: ${globalThis._fsIndex.size} files`);
  run_doc.target  = { data: [], meta: { total: globalThis._fsIndex.size } };
  run_doc.success = true;
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL — path resolution helpers
// ============================================================

async function _resolveParentDir(filePath) {
  const parts = filePath.split("/").filter(Boolean);
  parts.pop(); // remove filename
  let handle = globalThis._fsDirHandle;
  for (const part of parts) {
    handle = await handle.getDirectoryHandle(part, { create: false });
  }
  return handle;
}

async function _resolveHandleForWrite(filePath, create = false) {
  const parts = filePath.split("/").filter(Boolean);
  const fileName = parts.pop();
  let dirHandle = globalThis._fsDirHandle;
  for (const part of parts) {
    dirHandle = await dirHandle.getDirectoryHandle(part, { create });
  }
  return dirHandle.getFileHandle(fileName, { create });
}

// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================

globalThis.Adapters        = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.fs     = { init, select, create, update, delete: del, reindex };

criticise this as breaking architecture totally

2:47 PM
You're right — it breaks the architecture completely:

1. transform is not a CW operation — CW has select, create, update, delete. Adding transform means touching CW-run.js controller dispatch, _handlers, opConfig.type — ripple changes everywhere.

2. Adapters are storage connectors, not processors — Adapters.xlsx is not a storage adapter, it's a transformation library. Mixing concerns — the adapter registry now means two different things.

3. run_doc.script was your original idea — and it's architecturally correct. The script is a field on run_doc, the fs adapter calls it as part of update, the result flows through the chain to pb. No new operation type, no new adapter category, no controller changes.

4. The chain already works — ['fs', 'pocketbase'] for update. The script just runs inside fs.update before handing off to pb. That's the right layer — fs owns the file content, xlsx parsing is a file content operation.

So the correct architecture is:

javascript
CW.run({
  operation: 'update',
  target_doctype: 'File',
  query: { where: { extension: 'xlsx' } },
  script: CWXlsx.parse,  // ← runs inside fs.update
  options: { render: false }
})
CWXlsx is just a utility library, not an adapter. run_doc.script is the hook. No architecture changes needed.

now defend adapter

2:48 PM
The case for Adapters.xlsx:

1. Consistency — everything in CW goes through CW.run → adapter. If xlsx parsing is a bare function call outside the adapter system, it's a special case that breaks the "everything is a run" mental model.

2. Chainability — update: ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'] — xlsx sits between fs (reads file) and pb (persists result). The chain is the pipeline. No special script field needed, no new hook in fs.update.

3. Replaceability — tomorrow you want docx parsing, csv parsing, pdf parsing. They all register as adapters, slot into the chain at the same position. Adapters.docx, Adapters.csv. Config drives everything, no code changes.

4. run_doc.script is brittle — it's an ad-hoc escape hatch. Who sets it? When? What if two scripts needed? The adapter chain already solves sequencing cleanly.

5. transform operation is not needed — xlsx adapter just implements update(run_doc). It reads target.data[0], gets the file content from _fsIndex, parses it, writes ai_content back to target.data[0]. Same signature as every other adapter. No new operation type required.

The only real criticism is "adapters are storage connectors" — but CW never actually said that. Adapters are run_doc processors. Storage is just the most common use case.

2:52 PM
Yes. The schema drives it:

File schema has fields like ai_content, word_count, sheet_names etc — each field is an "outlet" for a specific extraction function.

xlsx adapter implements one function per field outlet:

javascript
Adapters.xlsx = {
  ai_content:   (run_doc) => ...,  // unpackXlsxToReadable
  sheet_names:  (run_doc) => ...,  // extract sheet names
  word_count:   (run_doc) => ...,  // count cells
  update:       async (run_doc) => {
    // run all field outlets that exist in schema
    const schema = CW.Schema?.File;
    for (const field of schema.fields) {
      if (Adapters.xlsx[field.fieldname]) {
        await Adapters.xlsx[field.fieldname](run_doc);
      }
    }
  }
}
Schema is the contract. Adapter implements the contract. Adding a new extracted field = add field to schema + add function to adapter. Nothing else changes.

2:54 PM
The adapter field on the schema field definition IS the wire. But we also need to tell CW which adapter handles the update chain for File.

Two levels of wiring:

Level 1 — doctype level (already have):

javascript
doctypeAdapters: {
  File: {
    select: 'fs',
    update: ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'],
  }
}
This tells CW to include xlsx in the update chain.

Level 2 — field level (schema):

json
{
  "fieldname": "ai_content",
  "adapter": "xlsx",
  "adapter_fn": "ai_content"
}
This tells Adapters.xlsx.update which function to call for which field.

The two levels are independent — level 1 routes the run to the xlsx adapter, level 2 tells the xlsx adapter what to do inside. Clean separation. The schema field definition is the contract between the doctype and the adapter function.

3:01 PM
No semantic issues — it's actually the cleanest possible convention:

javascript
Adapters.xlsx = {
  ai_content: async (run_doc) => { ... },   // fieldname = function name
  sheet_names: async (run_doc) => { ... },
  word_count:  async (run_doc) => { ... },
  update:      async (run_doc) => { ... },  // orchestrator
}
update iterates schema or _computed.xlsx keys, calls Adapters.xlsx[fieldname](run_doc) — direct lookup, no mapping needed.

One potential issue: update, select, create, delete are reserved operation names in the adapter registry — a field named update would collide with the operation handler.

So the constraint is: xlsx field names cannot be update, select, create, delete, init, reindex. Everything else is free. Reasonable constraint for field names.

3:06 PM
So the Adapter doctype has a scripts field — JSON array of CDN URLs to load before the adapter functions run. For xlsx adapter:

json
{
  "adapter_name": "xlsx",
  "scripts": ["https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/jszip@3.10.1/dist/jszip.min.js"],
  "functions": {
    "ai_content": "...",
    "sheet_names": "..."
  }
}
Boot loads the Adapter records from PocketBase, checks scripts, loads any missing CDN deps dynamically before registering the adapter functions.

This means CW-xlsx.js doesn't need to self-load JSZip — the Adapter record's scripts field handles that. The adapter record IS the deployment unit — scripts + functions in one pb document.

So Adapters.xlsx is not a static JS file but a compiled adapter from pb — same pattern as your existing Adapter doctype boot load.

This changes the question: should CW-xlsx.js be a static file at all, or should it be stored as an Adapter record in pb with scripts: ["jszip cdn"] and functions containing the parsed JS?

3:07 PM
Yes — mirrors the pb Adapter pattern exactly:

javascript
const XLSX_SCRIPTS = [
  'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/jszip@3.10.1/dist/jszip.min.js'
];

async function init(run_doc) {
  for (const src of XLSX_SCRIPTS) {
    if (typeof JSZip !== 'undefined') continue;
    await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
      const s = document.createElement('script');
      s.src = src;
      s.onload = resolve;
      s.onerror = reject;
      document.head.appendChild(s);
    });
  }
  run_doc.success = true;
}
Then _ensureInit pattern same as fs adapter — check if JSZip is available, call init if not. Every operation calls _ensureInit first.

CW-adapter-xlsx.js please

3:08 PM
javascript
// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-xlsx.js
// XLSX transform adapter — extracts computed fields from xlsx files
// Reads file content from _fsIndex via run_doc.target.data[0].name
// Writes results to run_doc.target.data[0]._computed.xlsx
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// ============================================================

const XLSX_SCRIPTS = [
  'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/jszip@3.10.1/dist/jszip.min.js'
];

// ============================================================
// INIT — load CDN dependencies if not already present
// ============================================================

async function _xlsxEnsureInit(run_doc) {
  if (typeof JSZip !== 'undefined') return true;
  await init(run_doc);
  return !run_doc.error;
}

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (typeof JSZip !== 'undefined') {
    run_doc.success = true;
    return;
  }
  try {
    for (const src of XLSX_SCRIPTS) {
      await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
        const s = document.createElement('script');
        s.src = src;
        s.onload = resolve;
        s.onerror = () => reject(new Error(`Failed to load: ${src}`));
        document.head.appendChild(s);
      });
    }
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL — get ArrayBuffer from _fsIndex
// ============================================================

async function _getBuffer(name) {
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex?.get(name);
  if (!rec) throw new Error(`File not in _fsIndex: ${name}`);
  const file = await rec._handle.getFile();
  return file.arrayBuffer();
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL — parse helpers
// ============================================================

function _parseXml(str) {
  return new DOMParser().parseFromString(str, 'application/xml');
}

async function _loadZip(buf) {
  return JSZip.loadAsync(buf);
}

async function _getSharedStrings(zip) {
  const f = zip.file('xl/sharedStrings.xml');
  if (!f) return [];
  const xml = _parseXml(await f.async('string'));
  return [...xml.querySelectorAll('si')].map(si =>
    [...si.querySelectorAll('t')].map(t => t.textContent).join('')
  );
}

async function _getSheetNames(zip) {
  const wbXml = _parseXml(await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml').async('string'));
  return [...wbXml.querySelectorAll('sheet')].map(s => s.getAttribute('name'));
}

function _resolveCell(c, strings) {
  const v = c.querySelector('v')?.textContent ?? '';
  const f = c.querySelector('f')?.textContent;
  const t = c.getAttribute('t');
  if (f) return `=${f}`;
  if (t === 's') return strings[parseInt(v)] ?? '';
  if (t === 'b') return v === '1' ? 'TRUE' : 'FALSE';
  return v;
}

function _colIndex(ref) {
  const col = ref.replace(/[0-9]/g, '');
  return [...col].reduce((n, c) => n * 26 + c.charCodeAt(0) - 64, 0) - 1;
}

// ============================================================
// FIELD FUNCTIONS — one per _computed.xlsx field
// Each receives (run_doc, zip, strings) — already parsed
// Writes to run_doc.target.data[0]._computed.xlsx[fieldname]
// ============================================================

async function ai_content(run_doc, zip, strings) {
  const sheetEls = [..._parseXml(await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml').async('string')).querySelectorAll('sheet')];
  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked excel file - resolved -->'];

  for (let si = 0; si < sheetEls.length; si++) {
    const sheetName = sheetEls[si].getAttribute('name');
    const sheetFile = zip.file(`xl/worksheets/sheet${si + 1}.xml`);
    if (!sheetFile) continue;

    const wsXml = _parseXml(await sheetFile.async('string'));
    const rows  = [...wsXml.querySelectorAll('row')];

    if (!rows.length) {
      parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si + 1}: ${sheetName} -->\n(empty)`);
      continue;
    }

    const grid = [];
    let maxCol = 0;
    for (const row of rows) {
      const r = parseInt(row.getAttribute('r')) - 1;
      const rowData = {};
      for (const c of row.querySelectorAll('c')) {
        const ci = _colIndex(c.getAttribute('r'));
        rowData[ci] = _resolveCell(c, strings);
        if (ci > maxCol) maxCol = ci;
      }
      grid[r] = rowData;
    }

    const headers = [];
    for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) {
      headers[c] = grid[0]?.[c] ?? String.fromCharCode(65 + c);
    }

    const colTypes = new Array(maxCol + 1).fill(null);
    for (let r = 1; r < grid.length; r++) {
      if (!grid[r]) continue;
      for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) {
        const v = grid[r][c];
        if (v === undefined || v === '') continue;
        const t = /^\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2}$/.test(v) ? 'date'
                : /^=/.test(v)                   ? 'formula'
                : isNaN(v)                        ? 'text'
                : 'number';
        if (colTypes[c] === null) colTypes[c] = t;
        else if (colTypes[c] !== t) colTypes[c] = 'mixed';
      }
    }

    const colTypeSummary = headers.map((h, i) => `${h}:${colTypes[i] ?? 'empty'}`).join(', ');
    parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si + 1}: ${sheetName} | columns: ${colTypeSummary} -->`);

    const lines = [];
    for (let r = 1; r < grid.length; r++) {
      if (!grid[r]) continue;
      const vals = [];
      for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) vals.push(grid[r][c] ?? '');
      lines.push(`${r + 1}: ${vals.join(' | ')}`);
    }
    parts.push(lines.join('\n'));
  }

  const doc = run_doc.target.data[0];
  if (!doc._computed) doc._computed = {};
  if (!doc._computed.xlsx) doc._computed.xlsx = {};
  doc._computed.xlsx.ai_content = parts.join('\n');
}

async function sheet_names(run_doc, zip) {
  const names = await _getSheetNames(zip);
  const doc = run_doc.target.data[0];
  if (!doc._computed) doc._computed = {};
  if (!doc._computed.xlsx) doc._computed.xlsx = {};
  doc._computed.xlsx.sheet_names = names;
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — orchestrator, calls all field functions
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _xlsxEnsureInit(run_doc)) return;

  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.name) {
    run_doc.error = '400 xlsx.update: no file record in target';
    return;
  }

  try {
    const buf     = await _getBuffer(doc.name);
    const zip     = await _loadZip(buf);
    const strings = await _getSharedStrings(zip);

    // call all registered field functions
    const ops = { ai_content, sheet_names };
    for (const [, fn] of Object.entries(ops)) {
      await fn(run_doc, zip, strings);
    }

    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================

globalThis.Adapters      = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.xlsx = { init, update, ai_content, sheet_names };

console.log('✅ CW-adapter-xlsx.js loaded');

  delete: 'fs',
}

3:37 PM
No it won't work well. The problem: xlsx adapter runs on EVERY File update — even when you're just updating a task status or renaming a file. You don't want xlsx parsing on every write.

The chain should be conditional — xlsx only runs when explicitly requested.

The real question is: when do you want xlsx parsing to run?

Two options:

Explicit operation — operation: 'transform' or a dedicated CW.run call that includes xlsx in the chain only when needed
Field-driven — xlsx runs only if run_doc.input or target.data[0] contains a request for _computed.xlsx fields
Option 2 fits your architecture best — xlsx adapter checks if _computed.xlsx is requested before doing any work:

javascript
async function update(run_doc) {
  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  // only run if _computed.xlsx explicitly requested
  if (!doc?._computed?.xlsx && !run_doc.options?.compute?.includes('xlsx')) return;
  ...
}
So config stays as ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'] but xlsx silently skips unless triggered. The trigger is either a flag in options.compute or presence of _computed.xlsx in the payload.

Which trigger do you prefer?

  target_doctype: 'File',
  operation: 'update',
  query: { where: { extension: 'xlsx' } },
  input: { ai_content: 'test ai extract' },
  options: { render: false }
}); will it process with current code

3:38 PM
No. The chain ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'] runs all three on every update. But xlsx adapter's update function tries to get ArrayBuffer from _fsIndex and parse the file — even when you're just writing ai_content: 'test ai extract' manually.

It will overwrite your manual ai_content with the parsed xlsx content. Wrong behavior.

The fix: keep xlsx OUT of the default chain. It should only run when explicitly called:

javascript
File: {
  select: 'fs',
  update: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],        // default — no xlsx
  create: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
  delete: 'fs',
  extract: ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'] // explicit extraction operation
}
Where extract is a new operation type — or more simply, caller passes options.adapters: ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'] to override the chain for that specific run.

Which approach fits better?

is not about config. its about of chain of calls and target.data

3:39 PM
Yes. The real problem is that after fs.update runs, it sets run_doc.target.data[0] to the merged fs record. Then xlsx.update receives that and tries to parse it as an xlsx file — but target.data[0] is just a metadata record with ai_content: 'test ai extract', not a file buffer.

Then pocketbase.update receives whatever xlsx.update left in target.data[0].

The chain corrupts target.data because each adapter overwrites it.

The fundamental issue: fs.update and xlsx.update both mutate target.data[0] for different purposes — fs for file metadata, xlsx for computed fields. They need to be aware of each other's output or run sequentially without clobbering.

The solution: xlsx.update should only ADD to _computed.xlsx inside target.data[0] — never replace the whole target. And it should only run when the file actually needs parsing — when _computed is absent or stale.

So the chain works if xlsx.update is purely additive — reads name from target.data[0], adds _computed.xlsx, leaves everything else untouched. Does your current xlsx.update do that?

lets start from the beginning WITHOUT xlsx adapter how const u = await CW.run({
  target_doctype: 'File',
  operation: 'update',
  query: { where: { extension: 'xlsx' } },
  input: { ai_content: 'test ai extract' },
  options: { render: false }
}); mutate target -> give faterfall in md

3:40 PM
CW.run()
  → CW.controller()
    → CW._resolveInput()
      target: null

    → pre-fetch select (operation swapped to 'select')
      → Adapters.fs.select()
        target: { data: [{ name, path, file_name, extension, ... }] }

    → CW._logChanges()     ← skipped (xlsx adapter has logChanges:0... wait, no xlsx yet)

    → CW._mergeInput()
      input: { ai_content: 'test ai extract' }
      target.data[0]: { name, path, ..., ai_content: 'test ai extract' }

    → CW._clearInput()

    → CW._handlers.update()
      → CW._preflight()
      → CW._stripVirtual()
      → loop: Adapters.fs.update()
          reads target.data[0].name → finds rec in _fsIndex
          no content → skips disk write
          merges metadata fields into _fsIndex
          target: { data: [full merged rec + ai_content], meta: { updated:1 } }
      → loop: Adapters.pocketbase.update()
          PATCH or POST target.data[0] to pb
          target: { data: [pb result], meta: { updated:1 } }
That's the clean working chain. Where do you want xlsx to slot in?

so basically xlsx needs fs to read file and needs pb to save file record with added fields

3:43 PM
Exactly. So xlsx sits between fs and pb:

→ Adapters.fs.update()
    target.data[0]: full rec + ai_content, meta: { updated:1 }

→ Adapters.xlsx.update()
    reads target.data[0].name → _fsIndex → ArrayBuffer
    parses xlsx
    ADDS to target.data[0]._computed.xlsx
    target.data[0]: same rec + _computed.xlsx added
    never replaces target, only adds

→ Adapters.pocketbase.update()
    persists target.data[0] including _computed.xlsx
The key constraint: xlsx only adds _computed.xlsx, never touches anything else in target.data[0]. fs result flows through unchanged, pb gets the enriched record.

This works with ['fs', 'xlsx', 'pocketbase'] — but only when xlsx parsing is actually needed. The skip condition inside xlsx.update is what controls it. Proceed?

3:44 PM
javascript
// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-xlsx.js
// Transform adapter — parses xlsx files, writes to _computed.xlsx
// Reads: _fsIndex via target.data[0].name
// Writes: target.data[0]._computed.xlsx — additive only, never replaces
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// ============================================================

const XLSX_SCRIPTS = [
  'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/jszip@3.10.1/dist/jszip.min.js'
];

// ============================================================
// INIT
// ============================================================

async function _xlsxEnsureInit(run_doc) {
  if (typeof JSZip !== 'undefined') return true;
  await init(run_doc);
  return !run_doc.error;
}

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (typeof JSZip !== 'undefined') { run_doc.success = true; return; }
  try {
    for (const src of XLSX_SCRIPTS) {
      await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
        const s = document.createElement('script');
        s.src = src; s.onload = resolve;
        s.onerror = () => reject(new Error(`Failed to load: ${src}`));
        document.head.appendChild(s);
      });
    }
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) { run_doc.error = err.message; }
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL HELPERS
// ============================================================

function _parseXml(str) {
  return new DOMParser().parseFromString(str, 'application/xml');
}

async function _getSharedStrings(zip) {
  const f = zip.file('xl/sharedStrings.xml');
  if (!f) return [];
  const xml = _parseXml(await f.async('string'));
  return [...xml.querySelectorAll('si')].map(si =>
    [...si.querySelectorAll('t')].map(t => t.textContent).join('')
  );
}

function _resolveCell(c, strings) {
  const v = c.querySelector('v')?.textContent ?? '';
  const f = c.querySelector('f')?.textContent;
  const t = c.getAttribute('t');
  if (f) return `=${f}`;
  if (t === 's') return strings[parseInt(v)] ?? '';
  if (t === 'b') return v === '1' ? 'TRUE' : 'FALSE';
  return v;
}

function _colIndex(ref) {
  const col = ref.replace(/[0-9]/g, '');
  return [...col].reduce((n, c) => n * 26 + c.charCodeAt(0) - 64, 0) - 1;
}

function _ensureComputed(doc) {
  if (!doc._computed)       doc._computed = {};
  if (!doc._computed.xlsx)  doc._computed.xlsx = {};
}

// ============================================================
// FIELD FUNCTIONS — additive writes to _computed.xlsx
// ============================================================

async function ai_content(run_doc, zip, strings) {
  const doc      = run_doc.target.data[0];
  const wbXml    = _parseXml(await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml').async('string'));
  const sheetEls = [...wbXml.querySelectorAll('sheet')];
  const parts    = ['<!-- unpacked excel file - resolved -->'];

  for (let si = 0; si < sheetEls.length; si++) {
    const sheetName = sheetEls[si].getAttribute('name');
    const sheetFile = zip.file(`xl/worksheets/sheet${si + 1}.xml`);
    if (!sheetFile) continue;

    const rows = [..._parseXml(await sheetFile.async('string')).querySelectorAll('row')];
    if (!rows.length) { parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si+1}: ${sheetName} -->\n(empty)`); continue; }

    const grid = []; let maxCol = 0;
    for (const row of rows) {
      const r = parseInt(row.getAttribute('r')) - 1;
      const rowData = {};
      for (const c of row.querySelectorAll('c')) {
        const ci = _colIndex(c.getAttribute('r'));
        rowData[ci] = _resolveCell(c, strings);
        if (ci > maxCol) maxCol = ci;
      }
      grid[r] = rowData;
    }

    const headers   = Array.from({ length: maxCol + 1 }, (_, c) => grid[0]?.[c] ?? String.fromCharCode(65 + c));
    const colTypes  = new Array(maxCol + 1).fill(null);
    for (let r = 1; r < grid.length; r++) {
      if (!grid[r]) continue;
      for (let c = 0; c <= maxCol; c++) {
        const v = grid[r][c];
        if (v === undefined || v === '') continue;
        const t = /^\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2}$/.test(v) ? 'date' : /^=/.test(v) ? 'formula' : isNaN(v) ? 'text' : 'number';
        colTypes[c] = colTypes[c] === null ? t : colTypes[c] !== t ? 'mixed' : t;
      }
    }

    parts.push(`\n<!-- sheet${si+1}: ${sheetName} | columns: ${headers.map((h,i) => `${h}:${colTypes[i]??'empty'}`).join(', ')} -->`);
    const lines = [];
    for (let r = 1; r < grid.length; r++) {
      if (!grid[r]) continue;
      lines.push(`${r+1}: ${Array.from({length: maxCol+1}, (_,c) => grid[r][c]??'').join(' | ')}`);
    }
    parts.push(lines.join('\n'));
  }

  _ensureComputed(doc);
  doc._computed.xlsx.ai_content = parts.join('\n');
}

async function sheet_names(run_doc, zip) {
  const doc      = run_doc.target.data[0];
  const wbXml    = _parseXml(await zip.file('xl/workbook.xml').async('string'));
  _ensureComputed(doc);
  doc._computed.xlsx.sheet_names = [...wbXml.querySelectorAll('sheet')].map(s => s.getAttribute('name'));
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — orchestrator
// Only runs if target.data[0] is an xlsx file
// Additive: only writes to _computed.xlsx, never replaces target
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _xlsxEnsureInit(run_doc)) return;

  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.name) return;

  // only process xlsx files
  if (doc.extension !== 'xlsx') return;

  // only run if _fsIndex has the file handle
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex?.get(doc.name);
  if (!rec) return;

  try {
    const file    = await rec._handle.getFile();
    const buf     = await file.arrayBuffer();
    const zip     = await JSZip.loadAsync(buf);
    const strings = await _getSharedStrings(zip);

    await ai_content(run_doc, zip, strings);
    await sheet_names(run_doc, zip);

    // success stays as set by previous adapter — don't overwrite
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================

globalThis.Adapters      = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.xlsx = { init, update, ai_content, sheet_names };

Key behaviors:

// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-dispatch.js
// Extension-based transform dispatcher.
// Reads target.data[0].extension → calls Adapters[ext].update(run_doc)
// Additive: never replaces target, only delegates to extension adapter
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  const ext = run_doc.target?.data?.[0]?.extension;
  if (!ext) return;

  const adapter = globalThis.Adapters[ext];
  if (!adapter?.update) return;

  await adapter.update(run_doc);
}

3:56 PM
Because init requires a user gesture to show the directory picker — it can't run automatically on page load. It's triggered by _ensureInit which is called by the first CW.run that hits the fs adapter.

But you got SELECT_FAILED not an init error — meaning _ensureInit ran, init completed, but then _fsIndex.values() failed. That means _fsIndex was created but then something cleared it.

This happens when init is called but the IDB restore failed silently and showDirectoryPicker was not triggered (no user gesture). _fsIndex gets initialized to new Map() but the walk never happens.

The _ensureInit check is:

javascript

_fsIndex is truthy (empty Map) but _fsDirHandle is falsy — so _ensureInit calls init again. But init checks:

if (globalThis._fsIndex && globalThis._fsDirHandle) return; // already initialized
Same check — _fsDirHandle is false so it proceeds. But no user gesture available for picker.

document what was done. how we chained adapters, how config works, what approached used, top2 problems we faced, key learnings

4:01 PM
CW Adapter Chain — Session Documentation
What Was Built
A multi-adapter chain system for the File doctype that routes a single CW.run call through multiple storage and transform layers in sequence.

How the Chain Works
CW._getAdapters(run_doc) resolves run_doc.adapter to a string array based on the operation:

javascript
CW._getAdapters = function(run_doc) {
  const a = run_doc.adapter;
  if (!a) return [CW._config.adapters.defaults.db];
  if (typeof a === 'string') return [a];
  if (Array.isArray(a)) return a;
  const resolved = a[run_doc.operation] || a['default'] || CW._config.adapters.defaults.db;
  return [].concat(resolved);
};
Handlers loop through the resolved array:

javascript
for (const a of CW._getAdapters(run_doc)) {
  await globalThis.Adapters[a][run_doc.operation](run_doc);
  if (run_doc.error) break;
}
Single run_doc flows through every adapter in sequence. Each adapter mutates run_doc.target.data[0] additively — never replacing what the previous adapter wrote.

Config
Per-operation adapter routing lives in doctypeAdapters:

javascript
doctypeAdapters: {
  File: {
    select: 'fs',
    update: ['fs', 'dispatch', 'pocketbase'],
    create: ['fs', 'pocketbase'],
    delete: 'fs',
  }
}
select — fs only (source of truth for file existence)
update — fs (metadata) → dispatch (extension router) → pocketbase (persist)
create — fs (write to disk) → pocketbase (commit record)
delete — fs only (hard delete from disk)
Adapter Architecture
4 adapters registered on globalThis.Adapters:

Adapter	Role
pocketbase	HTTP CRUD against PocketBase item collection
fs	File System Access API — _fsIndex in-memory handle registry
dispatch	Extension router — calls Adapters[ext].update(run_doc)
xlsx	Transform — parses xlsx, writes to target.data[0]._computed.xlsx
Mental model:

fs = working tree (live filesystem)
pocketbase File record = commit (intentional operation history, not directory mirror)
dispatch = extension point for new file types
xlsx/docx/pdf = transform adapters, purely additive
Adding a new file type: create CW-adapter-{ext}.js, register as Adapters.ext. Zero config changes, zero core changes.

Key Architectural Decisions
Stable File IDs — generateId("File", path) uses hashString(path) — deterministic, path-anchored, stable across sessions as long as same root folder is picked. Added PATH_KEYED to generateId alongside existing EMAIL_KEYED.

Pre-fetch select operation swap — controller pre-fetch uses run_doc.operation = 'select' temporarily so _getAdapters resolves adapter['select'] = 'fs' only, not the full update chain.

pb upsert — pb.update catch on 404 calls Adapters.pocketbase.create(run_doc) — first write creates the record, subsequent writes patch it. File record in pb is a commit, not a directory sync.

_computed pattern — transform adapters write to target.data[0]._computed.{adapter} — namespaced, never overwrites other adapters' data. Mirrors _state deep-merge discipline.

_logChanges adapter check — changed from every to some so logging skips when any adapter in the chain has logChanges: 0 (fs adapter opts out).

Top 2 Problems Faced
1. Global scope function name collision

Both pb-adapter-pocketbase.js and CW-adapter-fs.js define create, update, select, del as plain global functions. fs adapter loads after pb adapter — overwrites pb's functions in global scope. pb.update catch called bare create(run_doc) which resolved to fs create → tried to write a file instead of posting to PocketBase → "state cached" File System Access API error.

Fix: replace bare create(run_doc) call in pb.update catch with Adapters.pocketbase.create(run_doc) — resolves through registry, not global scope. Same fix for del calling update.

Long-term fix: wrap each adapter file in IIFE or convert to ES modules.

2. Pre-fetch select running wrong adapters

Controller pre-fetch block calls CW._handlers.select to load the record before update. But run_doc.operation is still 'update' at that point, so _getAdapters resolves adapter['update'] = ['fs', 'pocketbase']. fs returns the file record, then pb runs and returns empty (record doesn't exist yet), overwrites target.data with []. Controller then sees no name → routes to create → _preflight fails with "File requires a path".

Fix: swap run_doc.operation = 'select' before pre-fetch, restore after. One clean semantic fix — pre-fetch IS a select operation.

Key Learnings
Plain script files share global scope — any function declared at top level is global. Two adapter files with identical function names silently overwrite each other. Always call adapter functions via Adapters.X.fn() registry, never by bare name inside adapter files.

Adapter contract must be additive — each adapter in a chain should only add to target.data[0], never replace it. The pb adapter replacing target after a successful PATCH is correct (it returns the server's canonical record). Transform adapters (xlsx) must be purely additive — read name, write to _computed, leave everything else untouched.

Operation semantics are adapter-specific — update means "overwrite file" for fs, "upsert record" for pb, "parse and enrich" for xlsx. The operation name is the routing key; each adapter interprets it according to its own capabilities. The chain model handles this cleanly — no adapter needs to know what the others do.

File doctype is two-layer — fs owns existence and content (working tree), pb owns metadata and computed fields (commit history). name = hashString(path) is the join key between the two layers. reindex refreshes the working tree but never touches pb — pb records are intentional commits, not directory mirrors.

what this new approach gives us strategically

4:04 PM
1. File system becomes a first-class doctype

Files are now full CW documents — they have _state, _changes, _computed, ACL via _allowed. A file is not just a blob on disk, it's a document with history, permissions, and computed intelligence. This is the foundation for a browser-based notebook/IDE where every file is a queryable, versioned document.

2. Adapter chain = declarative pipeline

Storage, transformation, and persistence are separate concerns wired by config, not code. Adding pdf extraction = CW-adapter-pdf.js + nothing else. Swapping PocketBase for SQLite = change one config line. The pipeline is inspectable — every step is a named adapter, every result is in run_doc — debuggable via CW.runs.

3. AI-ready document corpus

_computed.xlsx.ai_content is the Step 0 probe output feeding AI code generation. Every file type gets its own extractor. The entire project directory becomes a structured, queryable knowledge base for AI — not raw files but parsed, resolved, token-efficient representations stored in PocketBase.

4. Offline-first with cloud sync

fs adapter is the working tree — works completely offline. pb adapter is the sync layer — commits when online. The chain naturally implements offline-first: fs always succeeds, pb fails gracefully and retries. This is git's model applied to documents.

5. Extension without modification

Every new capability — new file type, new storage backend, new transform — is a new file that registers itself. Core (CW-run.js, controller, handlers) never changes. The system grows by addition, not modification. This is the open/closed principle applied to the entire framework.

lets do identical adapter for pdf. the goal is to have ai_content as much structured as possible for AI esp like form data inside. advice the lib first

4:06 PM
For PDF specifically — form data, structured text, tables — the best browser-compatible options:

1. PDF.js (mozilla/pdf.js) — the gold standard. Extracts text with positional data, page structure, annotations. Can detect form fields. Used by every serious browser PDF tool. Large (~1MB) but comprehensive. Handles scanned PDFs via canvas rendering.

2. pdf-lib — focused on creation/manipulation, not extraction. Wrong tool for reading.

3. pdfminer.js / pdfjs-dist — same as PDF.js, pdfjs-dist is the npm package name.

Recommendation: pdfjs-dist for your use case because:

Extracts text with page/position structure — maps to <!-- page 1 --> format like your xlsx output
Form field extraction via getAnnotations() — AcroForm fields (name, value, type) directly accessible
Runs entirely in browser, no server
Same CDN pattern as JSZip
The output format for AI should mirror your xlsx approach:

<!-- page 1 -->
Company: Acme Corp
Date: 2024-01-15

<!-- page 2 | form fields -->
field: invoice_number | value: INV-001 | type: text
field: amount | value: 1500.00 | type: text
Structured, resolved, no noise. Shall I write CW-adapter-pdf.js?

yes

4:07 PM
javascript
// ============================================================
// CW-adapter-pdf.js
// Transform adapter — parses PDF files, writes to _computed.pdf
// Reads: _fsIndex via target.data[0].name
// Writes: target.data[0]._computed.pdf — additive only, never replaces
// All functions: function(run_doc) — mutate only, no return.
// ============================================================

const PDF_SCRIPTS = [
  'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/pdfjs-dist@4.4.168/build/pdf.min.mjs',
];

const PDFJS_WORKER = 'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/pdfjs-dist@4.4.168/build/pdf.worker.min.mjs';

// ============================================================
// INIT
// ============================================================

async function _pdfEnsureInit(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pdfjsLib) return true;
  await init(run_doc);
  return !run_doc.error;
}

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pdfjsLib) { run_doc.success = true; return; }
  try {
    // pdfjs-dist is an ES module — use dynamic import
    const pdfjs = await import(PDF_SCRIPTS[0]);
    pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = PDFJS_WORKER;
    globalThis.pdfjsLib = pdfjs;
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// INTERNAL HELPERS
// ============================================================

function _ensureComputed(doc) {
  if (!doc._computed)      doc._computed = {};
  if (!doc._computed.pdf)  doc._computed.pdf = {};
}

async function _loadPdf(buf) {
  const loadingTask = globalThis.pdfjsLib.getDocument({ data: buf });
  return loadingTask.promise;
}

async function _extractPageText(page) {
  const content = await page.getTextContent();
  // group spans into lines by y-position
  const lines = {};
  for (const item of content.items) {
    if (!item.str?.trim()) continue;
    const y = Math.round(item.transform[5]);
    if (!lines[y]) lines[y] = [];
    lines[y].push(item.str);
  }
  return Object.keys(lines)
    .sort((a, b) => b - a) // top to bottom
    .map(y => lines[y].join(' '))
    .filter(Boolean)
    .join('\n');
}

async function _extractFormFields(page) {
  const annotations = await page.getAnnotations();
  return annotations
    .filter(a => a.subtype === 'Widget')
    .map(a => ({
      field:    a.fieldName || a.alternativeText || '',
      value:    Array.isArray(a.fieldValue) ? a.fieldValue.join(', ') : (a.fieldValue || ''),
      type:     a.fieldType || 'text',
      required: !!a.required,
    }))
    .filter(f => f.field);
}

// ============================================================
// FIELD FUNCTIONS
// ============================================================

async function ai_content(run_doc, pdf) {
  const doc   = run_doc.target.data[0];
  const parts = ['<!-- unpacked pdf file - resolved -->'];

  for (let i = 1; i <= pdf.numPages; i++) {
    const page   = await pdf.getPage(i);
    const text   = await _extractPageText(page);
    const fields = await _extractFormFields(page);

    if (fields.length) {
      parts.push(`\n<!-- page ${i} | form fields -->`);
      for (const f of fields) {
        parts.push(`field: ${f.field} | value: ${f.value} | type: ${f.type}${f.required ? ' | required' : ''}`);
      }
      if (text) {
        parts.push(`\n<!-- page ${i} | text -->`);
        parts.push(text);
      }
    } else if (text) {
      parts.push(`\n<!-- page ${i} -->`);
      parts.push(text);
    } else {
      parts.push(`\n<!-- page ${i} -->\n(empty)`);
    }
  }

  _ensureComputed(doc);
  doc._computed.pdf.ai_content = parts.join('\n');
}

async function page_count(run_doc, pdf) {
  const doc = run_doc.target.data[0];
  _ensureComputed(doc);
  doc._computed.pdf.page_count = pdf.numPages;
}

async function form_fields(run_doc, pdf) {
  const doc    = run_doc.target.data[0];
  const fields = [];

  for (let i = 1; i <= pdf.numPages; i++) {
    const page        = await pdf.getPage(i);
    const pageFields  = await _extractFormFields(page);
    fields.push(...pageFields.map(f => ({ ...f, page: i })));
  }

  _ensureComputed(doc);
  doc._computed.pdf.form_fields = fields;
}

// ============================================================
// UPDATE — orchestrator
// Only runs if target.data[0] is a pdf file
// Additive: only writes to _computed.pdf, never replaces target
// ============================================================

async function update(run_doc) {
  if (!await _pdfEnsureInit(run_doc)) return;

  const doc = run_doc.target?.data?.[0];
  if (!doc?.name) return;

  // only process pdf files
  if (doc.extension !== 'pdf') return;

  // only run if _fsIndex has the file handle
  const rec = globalThis._fsIndex?.get(doc.name);
  if (!rec) return;

  try {
    const file = await rec._handle.getFile();
    const buf  = await file.arrayBuffer();
    const pdf  = await _loadPdf(buf);

    await ai_content(run_doc, pdf);
    await page_count(run_doc, pdf);
    await form_fields(run_doc, pdf);

  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

// ============================================================
// SELF-REGISTER
// ============================================================

globalThis.Adapters     = globalThis.Adapters || {};
globalThis.Adapters.pdf = { init, update, ai_content, page_count, form_fields };

console.log('✅ CW-adapter-pdf.js loaded');
Load order in HTML after CW-adapter-dispatch.js. No config changes needed — dispatch routes by extension automatically.

4:43 PM
pdfjsLib is undefined — init failed silently. The ES module dynamic import from CDN failed and the error was swallowed.

Two issues:

init sets run_doc.error but _pdfEnsureInit returns !run_doc.error — but update doesn't pass a real run_doc to _pdfEnsureInit at init time, it passes the actual run_doc which then gets its error cleared by the controller.
Dynamic import() of a .mjs from CDN may be blocked by CSP or CORS.
The reliable loading pattern — same as JSZip, script tag not dynamic import:

javascript
const PDF_SCRIPTS = [
  'https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/pdfjs-dist@4.4.168/build/pdf.min.js',  // UMD not ESM
];

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pdfjsLib) { run_doc.success = true; return; }
  try {
    await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
      const s = document.createElement('script');
      s.src = PDF_SCRIPTS[0];
      s.onload = resolve;
      s.onerror = () => reject(new Error(`Failed to load: ${PDF_SCRIPTS[0]}`));
      document.head.appendChild(s);
    });
    globalThis.pdfjsLib.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = PDFJS_WORKER;
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}
Use UMD .js not .mjs — loads as script tag, registers window.pdfjsLib globally. Proceed?

why u changed appraoch

4:44 PM
You're right. The approach should be identical to xlsx — script tag, same pattern, same reliability. The only difference was I used import() for pdf instead of script tag, which was wrong.

The xlsx pattern is the established one:

javascript
async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pdfjsLib) { run_doc.success = true; return; }
  try {
    for (const src of PDF_SCRIPTS) {
      await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
        const s = document.createElement('script');
        s.src = src;
        s.onload = resolve;
        s.onerror = () => reject(new Error(`Failed to load: ${src}`));
        document.head.appendChild(s);
      });
    }
    globalThis.pdfjsLib.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = PDFJS_WORKER;
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}
What's the correct UMD CDN URL for pdfjs-dist that registers window.pdfjsLib?

Option 1 — use v3 (last easy UMD)

<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/3.11.174/pdf.min.js"></script>
<script>
pdfjsLib.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc =
  'https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/3.11.174/pdf.worker.min.js';
</script>
This gives you:

4:47 PM
javascript
const PDF_SCRIPTS = [
  'https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/3.11.174/pdf.min.js'
];

const PDFJS_WORKER = 'https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/3.11.174/pdf.worker.min.js';

async function init(run_doc) {
  if (globalThis.pdfjsLib) { run_doc.success = true; return; }
  try {
    for (const src of PDF_SCRIPTS) {
      await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
        const s = document.createElement('script');
        s.src = src;
        s.onload = resolve;
        s.onerror = () => reject(new Error(`Failed to load: ${src}`));
        document.head.appendChild(s);
      });
    }
    globalThis.pdfjsLib.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = PDFJS_WORKER;
    run_doc.success = true;
  } catch (err) {
    run_doc.error = err.message;
  }
}

4:57 PM
Full IRS 1040 form extracted — form fields with values, page text, all structured. Working perfectly.

The field names are XFA-style paths (topmostSubform[0].Page1[0].f1_02[0]) — these are meaningful to AI for form understanding but could be simplified for human readability. That's a future improvement.

The pipeline is now:

xlsx → resolved tabular data with column types and row numbers
pdf → form fields with values + page text, page-separated
Both stored in _computed.{ext} in PocketBase, retrievable via CW.run select. Ready to feed into AI prompts as Step 0 probe output.

Next step: CW-adapter-docx.js?

now actually we have quite elegant processing status situation  as file. "_computed": {
    "pdf": {
      "ai_content":  not null means that its process with Adapter.pdf.ai_content funciton already

5:00 PM
Exactly. _computed.pdf.ai_content !== null is the processed flag — no separate status field needed.

The full status matrix falls out naturally:

_computed missing entirely     → never processed
_computed.pdf missing          → pdf adapter never ran
_computed.pdf.ai_content null  → ran but failed or empty
_computed.pdf.ai_content set   → processed successfully
Same pattern works for xlsx, docx, any future adapter. The _computed namespace IS the processing ledger — per adapter, per field, derived from data presence not a separate status flag.

This also means you can query PocketBase for unprocessed files:

javascript
CW.run({
  target_doctype: 'File',
  operation: 'select',
  query: { where: { '_computed': null } }  // never processed
})
Or reprocess specific files by clearing _computed.pdf and running update again. Clean.

what is missing on strategic level to become from files to knoledge management system

5:06 PM
The pipeline you have covers ingestion and extraction. What's missing for a full knowledge management system:

1. Search and retrieval _computed.ai_content is stored in PocketBase but not searchable by meaning — only by exact text match. Missing: vector embeddings of _computed content stored alongside the record, enabling semantic search ("find files about tax deductions" not just LIKE '%tax%'). PocketBase doesn't do vectors natively — needs a vector store (pgvector, Qdrant, or even local embeddings via transformers.js).

2. Relationships between documents Files are isolated records. Missing: cross-document links — "this xlsx references the same client as this pdf", "these two contracts are about the same entity". This is the graph layer on top of the document layer. Your Relationship doctype is already the right primitive — needs wiring to File.

3. Provenance and staleness _computed is a snapshot at processing time. If the file changes on disk, _computed is stale but there's no signal. Missing: _computed.{ext}.processed_at timestamp + comparison against rec.data.modified — stale detection built into the dispatch adapter.

4. Chunking for large files Large PDFs exceed LLM context. ai_content works for small files but breaks at scale. Missing: chunking strategy — split by page, section, or semantic boundary — stored as child records linked to the parent File.

5. Extraction quality feedback loop No way to know if the AI used _computed correctly or hallucinated. Missing: a _computed.{ext}.verified flag set when a human confirms the extraction was used correctly — closes the loop between extraction and consumption.

The first two are the highest leverage — search/retrieval turns a file archive into a queryable knowledge base, and relationships turn isolated documents into a connected graph.

Top 3 by stars and relevance to your use case:

1. MarkItDown (Microsoft) — ~50k stars, converts PDFs, Office documents, images, audio into clean Markdown, preserving headings, lists, tables and links — designed specifically for LLM ingestion. Supports xlsx, docx, pdf, pptx, html, images. The most broadly adopted. Python only — server-side. 
InfoWorld

2. Unstructured (~10k stars) — open-source ETL for ingesting PDFs, HTML, Word docs and more, partitioning each file into typed elements (Title, NarrativeText, Table, ListItem) with metadata including page numbers, coordinates, SHA hashes. Production RAG workhorse. Version 0.18 (summer 2025) added faster PDF partitioning and a revamped chunking API. Python only. 
GitHub
Substack

3. Docling (IBM) — supports PDF, images, markdown, Office, HTML and more — with LLM or VLM extraction backends, chunking, and export to CSV, Cypher and other knowledge-graph formats. Most architecturally ambitious — goes beyond extraction into graph relationships. Python only. 
GitHub

Key observation for your setup: all three are Python/server-side. Your approach of browser-native extraction (JSZip + PDF.js) is unique — no server required, works offline, integrates directly into CW's fs adapter chain. The tradeoff is you miss OCR (scanned PDFs) and layout ML (table detection). For native digital files — xlsx, form PDFs, docx — your approach is sufficient and faster.

for Web Speech API / Whisper.js how realistically i can do this browser

5:15 PM
Web Speech API — built into Chrome, no library needed. Works right now:

javascript
const recognition = new webkitSpeechRecognition();
recognition.continuous = true;
recognition.onresult = e => console.log(e.results);
recognition.start();
Limitations: live microphone only, no file input, no offline, Chrome-only, no transcript export. Useless for processing existing audio files.

Whisper.js (transformers.js) — runs OpenAI Whisper model in browser via WebAssembly/WebGPU. Realistic but heavy:

Model download: 150MB (tiny) to 1.5GB (small) on first load, cached in browser
Inference: 30s audio takes ~10-30s on modern laptop CPU, 3-5s on WebGPU
Works offline after first load
Supports file input — you can pass an ArrayBuffer from _fsIndex
Realistic verdict:

Small meeting recordings, voice memos under 5 minutes: feasible with tiny model
Long interviews, lectures: too slow without GPU
Production use: call Whisper API (OpenAI or local) from browser instead — 10x faster, same result
For your CW adapter pattern the realistic implementation is CW-adapter-audio.js that either runs transformers.js locally for short files or calls an OpenAI-compatible endpoint for longer ones — same run_doc contract, same _computed.audio.ai_content output.

Yes. Your Relationship doctype is already the right primitive.

Palantir's core idea simplified:

Every extracted entity becomes a document, every connection between entities becomes a Relationship.

From the 1040 you just extracted:

Person: Robin Brook (SSN: 222222222)

Robin Brook → EARNED → $42,000

What's missing vs Palantir:

Entity resolution — same person appearing in multiple documents gets merged into one record, not duplicated

Graph query — "show all people connected to this address" across all documents
The _computed output you already have is the perfect input for step 2 — feed it to Claude, get back entities and relationships as JSON, create CW records via CW.run. The graph emerges from your existing Relationship doctype naturally.

how palantir prepolulating ontologys,

5:20 PM
Palantir's core pattern — called Ontology-Driven Integration:

1. Schema first, data second

They define object types before ingesting data:

Person { name, ssn, dob, address }
Organization { name, ein, type }
Transaction { amount, date, currency }
The ontology is the contract. Data sources map INTO it, not the other way around.

2. Transforms — not extraction, mapping

Raw data (CSV, PDF, database row) → transform function → typed object. The transform is deterministic and repeatable. Same source file always produces the same objects. Your _computed.pdf.ai_content is the raw data, the transform maps it to Person, Address etc.

3. Direct Object Identifier (DOI)

Every object has a stable ID derived from its natural key — SSN for Person, EIN for Organization, address string for Address. Same as your hashString(path) for File. This enables entity resolution — same SSN in two documents = same Person object, automatically merged.

4. Links are first-class

Relationships between objects are stored separately from the objects themselves — same as your Relationship doctype. The graph is the product, not a side effect.

Applied to your stack:

_computed.pdf.ai_content          ← raw
     ↓ Claude API call
{ entities: [...], links: [...] } ← transform output  
     ↓ CW.run create
Person, Address, Relationship     ← ontology objects in PocketBase
Your Relationship doctype + generateId(doctype, naturalKey) for stable IDs + Claude for extraction = Palantir's core loop, browser-native.

how palantir structures the graph

6:14 PM
Palantir's graph has three layers:

1. Objects — typed nodes, each with stable ID derived from natural key:

Person/222222222        → { name, ssn, dob }
Address/1519DensonAve  → { street, city, state, zip }
Document/f1040.pdf     → { file_name, date, type }
Income/222222222-2022  → { amount, year, source }
2. Links — typed edges, always directional, always between two specific object types:

Person → FILED → Document
Person → LIVES_AT → Address  
Person → MARRIED_TO → Person
Person → EARNED → Income
Person → PARENT_OF → Person
Links are not free-form — they are defined in the ontology schema. Person → LIVES_AT → Address is a valid link type. Person → LIVES_AT → Income is not.

3. Properties — time-series aware. Every property value has a timestamp. Address changes over time — Palantir stores the full history:

Person/222222222.address:
  2020: "100 Main St"
  2022: "1519 Denson Ave"  ← current
Applied to your stack exactly:

Object type    → CW doctype (Person, Address, Organization)
Link type      → Relationship with type field
Stable ID      → generateId(doctype, naturalKey)
Properties     → doc.data fields
History        → _changes append-only audit trail  ← you already have this
Your _changes field IS Palantir's time-series property store. You already have the full architecture. What's missing is just the extraction step that creates the objects from _computed.

do they anonimize unique ids like ssn or use them diretly in data model

6:16 PM
Palantir uses them directly in the data model internally — SSN, EIN, passport numbers are the natural keys for entity resolution. The whole point is that the same SSN across two documents = same person = merge.

But they separate three concerns:

1. Storage — raw SSN stored encrypted at rest, access-controlled per object type. The SSN is the key but never exposed in queries or UI unless you have explicit permission.

2. Object ID — a derived, non-reversible hash of the natural key:

Person ID = hash("Person" + "222222222")  ← same as your hashString
The ID is used everywhere in the graph. The raw SSN is stored separately behind ACL. Someone with graph access sees the node, not the SSN.

3. ACL at object level — your _allowed / _allowed_read fields on the CW record. A Person object has _allowed_read: ["analysts"] but SSN field has _allowed_read: ["compliance"]. Field-level permissions, not just record-level.

Applied to your stack:

Person record in PocketBase:
  name: "file01p9g9qt7yc"  ← hashString("Person", ssn) — the ID
  data: {
    display_name: "Robin Brook",
    ssn_hash: hashString("SSN", "222222222"),  ← for resolution only
    ssn_encrypted: "...",                       ← behind strict ACL
    first_name: "Robin",
    last_name: "Brook"
  }
  _allowed_read: ["system_manager"]
  _allowed: ["system_manager"]
The SSN never appears in the graph traversal — only in the raw data field behind ACL. Your existing _allowed / _allowed_read systemFields already implement this pattern. You just need field-level ACL on top of record-level ACL — one additional layer.

how relaible my hash from backwards guessing

6:19 PM
Not reliable at all for SSN. Here's why:

SSN space is tiny

SSN is 9 digits → 10^9 = 1 billion possible values. An attacker doesn't need to reverse your hash — they just brute-force all 1 billion SSNs through hashString and look up the result in a rainbow table. On modern hardware that takes minutes.

Your hashString (MurmurHash-style) is designed for speed — it hashes millions of values per second. Speed is exactly what you don't want for sensitive identifiers.

The fix — slow hash with salt:

javascript
async function hashSensitive(value, salt = 'cw-ontology-v1') {
  const encoder = new TextEncoder();
  const keyMaterial = await crypto.subtle.importKey(
    'raw', encoder.encode(salt), { name: 'PBKDF2' }, false, ['deriveBits']
  );
  const bits = await crypto.subtle.deriveBits(
    { name: 'PBKDF2', salt: encoder.encode(value), iterations: 100000, hash: 'SHA-256' },
    keyMaterial, 128
  );
  return btoa(String.fromCharCode(...new Uint8Array(bits))).slice(0, 15);
}
PBKDF2 with 100k iterations — brute-forcing 1 billion SSNs now takes years not minutes. Built into browser via crypto.subtle, no library needed.

Two-hash pattern:

generateId("Person", path) — your current fast hash, fine for file paths (not sensitive)
hashSensitive(ssn) — slow hash for SSNs, EINs, passport numbers
Use hashSensitive only for natural keys derived from PII. Everything else stays on generateId.

why crypto.subtle not used for my has

6:20 PM
Because generateId was designed for document naming, not security. Its requirements are:

Fast — called thousands of times during _walkDir indexing
Readable prefix — filesr c... not a random string
Deterministic — same input same output
Short — exactly 15 chars to fit CW name convention
None of these are security requirements. File paths, doctype names, email addresses for User IDs — none of this is sensitive PII. Collision resistance at 36^11 space is sufficient for uniqueness within a project.

crypto.subtle would be wrong for generateId because:

PBKDF2 is async — generateId is sync, called inside _walkDir loop
100k iterations × 1000 files = indexing takes minutes not seconds
Output is base64 not alphanumeric — breaks the 15-char name convention
The split is clean:

generateId(doctype, path)      → fast, sync, for document IDs
hashSensitive(ssn)             → slow, async, for PII natural keys
When you build the ontology extraction layer — Person, Address etc — hashSensitive is the right tool for those object IDs. generateId stays unchanged for everything else.

i mean inside for like user type for email

6:20 PM
Good catch. EMAIL_KEYED uses hashString(email) for User IDs:

javascript
return (EMAIL_KEYED[doctype] + hashString(title)).substring(0, 15);
Email space is much larger than SSN — billions of possible addresses — but still enumerable if an attacker has a known list of emails. Corporate directory + hashString → rainbow table in minutes.

However for User IDs the threat model is different:

The hash is stored as the name field in PocketBase — visible to anyone with record access
If they have record access they likely already have the email (it's stored in data.email)
The hash is used for record lookup and relationships, not as a secret
So the question is: what are you protecting?

If the concern is "don't expose email in the ID field" — hashString is fine, it's not reversible by casual inspection.

If the concern is "prevent a determined attacker with PocketBase read access from recovering emails" — then crypto.subtle is needed.

For your current use case (internal tool, authenticated users, email already stored in data) — hashString is acceptable. The email is not a secret in your system.

For the ontology/PII case (SSN, passport, EIN stored as natural keys) — hashSensitive is required because those values ARE secrets even from internal users with partial access.

crypto.subtle how fast is this

6:21 PM

// INIT
// INPUT

const salt = 'cw-ontology-v1';

// test 1 hash time

const keyMaterial = await crypto.subtle.importKey(
  'raw', encoder.encode(salt), { name: 'PBKDF2' }, false, ['deriveBits']
);
const bits = await crypto.subtle.deriveBits(
  { name: 'PBKDF2', salt: encoder.encode(email), iterations: 100000, hash: 'SHA-256' },
  keyMaterial, 128
);

console.log('1000 hashes estimate:', ((t2-t1) * 1000 / 1000).toFixed(1), 'seconds');
console.log('result:', btoa(String.fromCharCode(...new Uint8Array(bits))).slice(0, 15));
Run this — the number will tell you if it's viable for your use case. Typical range is 50-500ms per hash depending on device.
